C. RISKS AND SENSITIVITY ANALYSIS
5.13    Project Risks: The project is a 'high reward-high risk' venture. The project in general and the
institutional reforms in particular if implemented, would provide enormous benefits as outlined earlier.
These reforms represent the only solution to ensure the long-term sustainability of the irrigation and
drainage system and the agriculture sector of Pakistan. However, the project also has very significant risks.
These risks, as well as the risk-mitigation and risk-management factors/strategies53, are discussed below
under the following headings: (i) derailment of the institutional reform program; (ii) slow or imperfect
formation of FOs; and (iii) sustainability of investments in irrigation and drainage infrastructure.
5.14    Derailment of the Institutional Reform Program: As is inherent in any major reform program,
the institutional reforms supported by the project carry very significant risks. The proposed institutional
reforms would significantly affect the existing power relationships and alliances in rural Pakistan. While
the reforms largely seek 'win-win' situations, the perceived (and in part, real) threat of loss of control over
the system, particularly by feudal landlords who are unaccustomed to sharing water and power, and by
irrigation bureaucrats with financial ties to these interests, who stand to benefit from the continuation of the
institutional status quo, could provoke strong adverse reactions. Large and povverful landlords view the
proposed transformation of PIDs into autonomous PIDAs and AWBs, the formation of FOs and the
transfer of management responsibilities of the tertiary system to these FOs, and the establishment of water
rights as potential threats to their traditional control over the irrigation and drainage system in particular,
and the social structure (feudal system) in general. Some sections of the PIDs, which when transformed
would be faced with a hard budget constraint, more accountability, financial transparency and scrutiny, and
possibly reduced costs and staffng, view the reforms as threats to their power, authority and rent-seeking
opportunities. Similarly, the proposed strategic reorientation of WAPDA which seeks to transform
WAPDA's role from large-scale construction to knowledge-based RBM, and the progressive transfer of its
construction activities in intra-provincial and on-farm infrastructure to PIDAs, AWBs and FOs, is viewed
53      Risk-mitigation factors/measures are factors/measures to reduce the probability of risk; while risk-
management strategies are measures which would be taken to minimize loss if the risk materializes.



41
by some officials as a diminution in WAPDA's role in management of the irrigation and drainage system.
There is a risk that these vested interests (who have very significant political and financial clout) would
slow, or even stop, reform. The proposed reforms have already provoked strong adverse reactions from
these opponents in the form of spreading misinformation, organizing political opposition, and bureaucratic
delays and stalling tactics including continuous whittling down of reform proposals at various stages.
5.15    Risk-mitigation: Demonstration of strong political commitment and leadership by the Borrower,
Provinces, and WAPDA to follow through with the institutional reforms, especially regarding
decentralization and management transfer of the irrigation and drainage system is crucial to mitigating this
risk. So far, this has been forthcoming. The ownership for the reforms at the highest levels is strong
especially since the institutional reform strategy was formulated by the Borrower based on its assessment
of the reforms' likely ownership by the people of Pakistan and chances of success in Pakistan's
environment. The reform program was first endorsed at the highest political levels on August 19, 199554;
and has been repeatedly re-endorsed at similar levels on several occasions by three successive
Governments (Federal and Provincial) since then, sometimes in the face of mounting opposition from
organized groups (notably large landholders, feudal landlords, and some officials of PIDs). The Borrower
and Provinces engaged in extensive consultations with the various stakeholders (including politicians,
organized farmer groups, Chambers of Agriculture, Provincial Departments, etc.) to build consensus and
win acceptance of the reform program, including on the PIDA Acts. The political and wide-ranging
support for the reform program was most recently demonstrated in the approval of the PIDA Acts by all the
four Provincial Assemblies and the reenactment of the PIDA Acts55. The extensive debate on the reform
strategy, wide-ranging consultations, and the resulting education about the reforms have lowered the
perceived threats of the reforms to some degree. The project's risk mitigation strategy is: (i) to continue to
encourage political debate about irrigation policy in Pakistan, and thereby help build both conscious top-
level political ownership and widespread support among the various stakeholders for the reform program;
(ii) strengthen the constituency for reforms through extensive technical assistance, communication and
beneficiary participation programs; and (iii) establish institutional focal points in the Federal Government
(e.g.: the FIDC), WAPDA (e.g.: NDP Coordination Cell, and possible Institutional Change Department),
and Provinces (e.g.: NDP Cells, transition wings in PIDAs and AWBs, and FOs) and provide technical
assistance to create the necessary incentives and mandates, and equip them with resources/capacity to
function as agents for institutional change. In spite of these measures, real institutional reform is by no
means assured. There is the danger that the PIDAs and AWBs could be captured by corrupt and
incompetent officials, and that the PIDAs and AWBs would lack the operational and financial autonomy to
function as effective institutions".
5.16    Risk-management Strategy: The project's risk management strategy (in the event that all or part
of the risk materializes) is two-fold: (i) IDA would only finance those PAs and Investment Projects which
conform to the institutional reform strategy. Specifically, the eligibility criteria for PAs provide for each
PIDA, AWB and FO to be eligible for incremental financing commitments only if it is established and
operated as an autonomous entity; and the selection criteria for Investment Projects provide for Investment
Projects to be financed only if they are carried out by PAs which have operational jurisdiction over the
Investment Project; (ii) the Borrower and IDA have agreed and understand that IDA's incremental
financing commitments for irrigation and drainage investments under NDP would be scaled back or
canceled altogether after the MTR if the pace of reforms is slow due to lack of government commitment,
implementation constraints, or resistance/lack of commitment by WAPDA, PIDAs or AWBs for real
change.
54     At a meeting involving the President, Prime Minister, the four Provincial Chief Ministers, Cabinet officials,
and Secretaries from the Borrower and all the four Provinces.
55     In the absence of Provincial Assemblies, the PIDA Statutes were originally promulgated as Ordinances in all
the four Provinces; and reenacted by the Provincial Assemblies after the general elections in February 1997.
56     Although the PIDA Acts have several provisions to ensure autonomy of PIDAs and AWBs.



42
5.17    Slow  or Imperfect Formation and Functioning of FOs: Effective FOs will ultimately be
essential for the financial sustainability of the irrigation and drainage system. FOs are crucial not only for
assuming responsibilities for O&M of the tertiary system (i.e., on-farm drainage and irrigation upto the
minor/distributary level), but more importantly to ensure that that the AWBs and PIDAs are held
accountable for service delivery, maintenance of physical structures, and assessment of charges, and to
bring user discipline to water distribution. However, there is a risk that formation of FOs may be very slow
especially since the proposed FOs are to be established in a highly differentiated environment with respect
to land ownership, water rights and economic needs, and with a mixed record from Water Users
Associations and farmers' cooperatives. Feudal landlords could use their existing social power-hold to
frustrate social mobilization efforts and prevent formation of FOs. There is also a risk that the proposed
FOs could be dominated by feudal landlords, and thereby ineffective. Finally, there is a risk of legal
impediments that prevent the FOs from taking over management responsibilities for the tertiary system.
The loss in terms of equity, cost recovery, and ensuring accountability would be significant, and their
impacts on O&M of the system (through losses on service quality and cost :recovery) would also be
significant. In addition, slow formation of FOs would also disrupt the strategy to improve O&M of the
tertiary system by transferring responsibility to user groups. This would directly affect the fiscal savings
expected to be achieved through the project (estimated to be about Rs. 2.5 billion or US$62 million at
completion).
5.18    Risk-mitigation and Risk-management: The risk-mitigation factors are detailed below: (i) the
most important factor mitigating this risk is the expected encouragement from positive results of on-going
pilots of FOs. These pilots would also help to reduce the perceived threats to the i nterests of the opponents
of reforms in the sector. The early results from these pilot projects indicate that FOs are socially viable i.e.,
with appropriate social engineering techniques, it is possible to form user groups in the prevailing socio-
cultural and political environment. The pilots have also identified a need for these user groups to be
empowered and authorized to carry out economic activities i.e., to manage the tertiary level system57. The
project's farmer participation plan includes a special effort to replicate lessons from current pilots, and to
implement early action plans to build FOs; (ii) the selection criteria for Investment Projects provides an in-
built incentive for formnation of FOs (since the selection criteria specifies that on-farm drainage and
irrigation upto the minor/ distributary level would be carried out by FOs); (iii) the project's social
mobilization activities and awareness initiatives, the front-end cost-sharing arrangements for investments
(which would necessarily require consultation with beneficiaries), and assistance to the private sector for
providing contracting services for on-farm subsurface drainage facilities, would facilitate formation of
FOs; and (iv) the PIDA Acts clearly define the roles and responsibilities of FOs which include the
management of the tertiary system. The risk management strategy is the same as that indicated in para 5.16
above.
5.19    Quantitative Assessment of Political-Economy Risk:  A quantitative risk assessment of the
major institutional reforms was conducted58. This consisted of: (i) an evaluation of the potential winners
and losers from the reforms; (ii) identification of the various reform performance levels; (iii) identification
of means by which the various parties could influence the level of achievement of various reforms; and
(iv) identification of costs to (i.e., effort required by) each party to influence the achievement levels; and
thereafter using the Delphi approach to estimate probabilities of level of achievement of each reform. This
analysis indicated that the reform performance levels are likely to vary across reforms. The most likely
scenario is a medium level of (partial) achievement on reforms relating to: (i) institutional reforms in PIDs;
(ii) transfer of management responsibilities of the tertiary system to FOs; (iii) redefining the operational
jurisdictions of various PAs; and (iv) carrying out O&M through Performance Contracts awarded to the
private sector; and a low level of achievement on establishment of water rights.
57      These lessons are drawn from the pilot project for farmer-managed irrigated agriculture under the LBOD
Project with technical assistance from IIMI (Moving Towards Participatory Irrigation Management - Phase II Report,
January 1997, IIMI).
58      Institutional Reforms in the Water Sector in Pakistan - Political Economy and Political Risk, Working Paper
for the National Drainage Program, May 1997.



43
5.20   Sustainability of Investments in Irrigation and Drainage Infrastructure: Experience has
demonstrated that the key requirement for sustainability of irrigation and drainage projects in Pakistan is a
steady-state post-completion O&M regime, with a reliable source of funding. As indicated earlier, the
proposed policy and institutional reforms are the most significant assurance for sustainability of
investments. There is however a risk that given that the institutional reforns may take many years to be
fully effective, the gains of the investments made in the interim period may not be sustainable, if real
institutional reform does not take place. To mitigate this risk, the project's design provides for institutional
reforms to precede investments in irrigation and drainage infrastructure.  Each Investment Project
(designed on a basin or sub-basin approach with a proper outfall) would virtually be a 'stand-alone'
investment. A reduction in the overall level of investments would not affect the economic viability of the
entire project. A related issue for sustainability of the system is a long-term solution for disposal of
drainage effluent outside the Indus Basin. The project would support the preparation of feasibility studies
and detailed design for the Borrower's proposed NSDS which is intended to create a permanent disposal
channel for drainage effluent via the LBOD into the Arabian Sea.
5.21   Implementation Delays: The other main risk to the project during its implementation phase is
slow implementation due to factors such as poor coordination, weak supervision, delays in preparation of
Investrnent Projects, delays in approval of contracts and investment projects, and failure of PAs to meet
eligibility criteria on schedule. To reduce these risks, authority and responsibility have been decentralized
significantly to PAs. The project is embedded in broad-based capacity building efforts for WAPDA,
PIDAs, AWBs, FOs, and PAD-OFWMs; and its design provides for extensive supervision and
implementation assistance. Finally, there are built-in mechanisms to ensure that there is a high degree of
client participation in the formulation and implementation of all the studies and research contracts. To
reduce the risks of delay, the contract with the NDP Engineering Design and Supervision Consultants (who
would assist substantially in the preparation of Investment Projects) has been signed. Contracts for civil
works which would be carried out in the first year have been signed or are in an advanced stage (post bid-
evaluation) of procurement processing. Several research contracts are also in an advanced stage of
procurement processing and are expected to be signed before Effectiveness.
5.22   Sensitivity Analysis for Investment Projects: The illustrative economic analysis carried out for
a sample of the project's interventions demonstrated that the economic viability of the Investment Projects
is fairly robust. Sensitivity analyses were undertaken to determine the effects on economic viability of: (i)
delays in project benefits resulting from slow implementation; (ii) increases in project costs resulting from
inefficient management and other factors; (iii) lower than predicted yields for major crops; and (iv) lower
prices for major commodity outputs; and (v) a shorter duration of project benefits. The analysis indicated
that the economic viability would be affected only with large adverse changes in these variables.
D. KEY INDICATORS AND MONITORING AND EVALUATION
5.23    Key Performance Indicators: Key Performance Indicators are presented in Annex 10. These
include input and process indicators, output indicators, and outcome and impact indicators for all
components of the project. The Borrower would maintain policies and procedures adequate to enable it to
monitor and evaluate on an on-going basis, in accordance with these indicators, the carrying out of the
Project and achievement of its objectives.
5.24   Monitoring and Evaluation (M&E): The M&E program would: (i) focus on key performance
indicators; (ii) cover the entire Indus Basin; and (iii) adopt an unified approach encompassing physical,
socio-economic, and environmental parameters. A number of baseline surveys and compilation of data
from recent surveys on salinity, agro-ecological conditions, and socio-economic conditions would be
conducted in the initial period of project implementation. The monitoring program would include
continuous assessment of project implementation in relation to agreed schedules; use of inputs,
infrastructure, and services by project beneficiaries; physical parameters such as depth-to-watertable and



44
soil salinity; client assessment of the institutional programs; and socio-economic benefits to the farming
community from project interventions. It would be an integral part of the project's management. Its main
objectives would be to provide continuous feedback on implementation, and to identify actual or potential
successes and problems as early as possible to facilitate timely adjustments to project operation. The
purpose of the evaluation program would be to provide periodic assessment of the relevance, performance,
efficiency, and impact (both expected and unexpected) of the project in relation to its stated objectives. The
M&E Program would include the Annual Review, MTR, ICR and Impact Evaluation. The MTR of the
project (including the functioning of the PIDAs, AWBs and FOs) would be completed not later than
December 31, 2000. The MTR would review progress of the first three years of project implementation
and provide a diagnosis of the likely effects of the project. It would identify project design and
implementation problems, re-evaluate the objectives, strategies, and targets, and propose solutions. The
Implementation Completion Report (ICR) would be completed not later than six months after the Closing
Date of the Project. Assurances were obtained at Negotiations that the Borrower would prepare the
Impact Evaluation Report for the project within three years of the project's Closing Date.
5.25    WAPDA, through its proposed Monitoring and Research Division, will coordinate M&E
arrangements. WAPDA would establish and maintain an effective M&E organization and system for the
project as a whole. In order to take advantage of the experience and capacities of various institutions
which have undertaken or have capability for monitoring, evaluation, and research in irrigation, drainage,
and socio-economic impact, WAPDA would establish collaborative arrangements with various institutions
such as provincial institutes, universities, and research institutes and NGOs (e.g. Applied Economic
Research Center, Sindh Development Studies Center, Punjab Economic Research Institute, Punjab
Irrigation Institute, Sindh Agricultural Research Institute, Pakistan Institute of Development Economics,
Faisalabad University, and selected PRIs). WAPDA would engage consultants as needed to assist in the
M&E program including design of the M&E program, capacity building and training for the M&E units of
the PAs (notably provincial institutes, WAPDA's Watercourse Monitoring and Evaluation Directorate,
WAPDA's SCARPs Monitoring Organization, etc.). Assurances were obtained at Negotiations that
WAPDA would engage M&E Consultants with qualifications and terms of reference satisfactory to IDA by
June 30, 1998.
6. AGREEMENTS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
A. CONDITIONS OF EFFECTIVENESS
6.1    Cofinancing: Fulfillment of Conditions of Effectiveness of the ADB Loan and the OECF Loan
(para 3.5).
B. OTHER IMPORTANT CONDITIONS
6.2    Conditions of Incremental Financing Commitments: The Borrower would, not later than April
30 of each Fiscal Year of project implementation, or such later date as IDA may agree, beginning Fiscal
Year 96-97, furnish to IDA for its approval, proposals for amounts to be allocated out of the proceeds of
the Credit for financing any new program of activities to be commenced under the project in the next
following year of project implementation. IDA would not approve any proposals furnished to it unless and
until:
(a)    the Borrower has, with the participation of WAPDA and the Provinces, prepared and
furnished to IDA:
(i)    a consolidated APR on the carrying out of the programs of activities previously
commenced under the Project;



45
(ii)    a Three-Year Rolling PSDP for the project for the next three following Fiscal
Years of project implementation;
(iii)    a Portfolio Action Plan for the project for the next following Fiscal Year of
project implementation; and
(iv)    a Three-Year Rolling Business Plan for the project, which would also include
procurement and disbursement targets, for the next three following Fiscal Years
of project implementation; and
(b)    IDA is satisfied with the progress made in the carrying out of:
(i)    the programs of activities previously commenced under the project; and
(ii)   the current Portfolio Action Plan and Three-Year Rolling Business Plan for the
project (para 3.11).
6.3    Sector Planning and Studies Consultants: WAPDA would engage sector planning and studies
consultants with qualifications and terms of reference satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998 (para 2.10).
6.4    Establishment of AWBs: Provinces would establish at least one AWB in a canal command in
each Province, selected in consultation with IDA, within one year of the establishment of the PIDA (para
2.24).
6.5    Selection Criteria for Investment Projects: Investment Projects financed under the project
would meet Selection Criteria (para 2.29 and Annex 1).
6.6    Detailed Designs and Award of Contracts for Investment Projects: WAPDA and Provinces
would complete all detailed designs and award contracts for Investment Projects so as to ensure that all
such contracts, including the maintenance period specified in such contracts, will be completed not later
than December 31, 2003 (para 2.35).
6.7    Participation Agreements: Provinces would enter into Participation Agreements, satisfactory to
IDA, with each PIDA, AWB and FO proposing to participate in the Project (para 3.10 and Annex 3).
6.8    Eligibility Criteria for PAs: Each PA would satisfy the specified eligibility criteria to be eligible
for incremental annual financing commitments from IDA Credit for new programs of activities to be
commenced under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for on-going Investment Projects
(para 4.2 and Annex 6).
6.9    Approval of Programs and Investment Projects: Institutional reform programs, research and
sector planning programs, Investment Projects, and program coordination and supervision activities
fnanced from the IDA Credit would be approved by IDA (para 4.3).
6.10   WAPDA and Provincial Coordination: (i) WAPDA would maintain for the duration of the
project an NDP Coordination Cell in WAPDA's Water Wing with organization, terms of reference and
staff satisfactory to IDA; (ii) Each Province would maintain for the duration of the project, a Provincial
NDP Coordination Cell, with organization, terms of reference and staff satisfactory to IDA; and (iii) the
NDP Cells in WAPDA and Provinces would be headed by an NDP Program Coordinator and Provincial,
NDP Coordinators respectively whose rank, qualifications, authority, and responsibilities would be
satisfactory to IDA (para 4.6).
6.11    Financial Management, Accounts and Audit: (i) WAPDA would engage FMIS consultants with
qualifications and terms of reference satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998; (ii) adequate records and
accounts to reflect, in accordance with sound accounting practices, the operations, resources and
expenditures in respect of the project would be maintained; and (iii) the NDP Coordination Cell would



46
submit the audit reports for the consolidated fnancial statements of the project to IDA not later than six
months after the close of each fiscal year (para 4.8).
6.12   Supervision Plan: The Borrower would: (i) submit the Quarterly Progress Report of the Project
within one month of the end of each Quarter; and (ii) prepare a MTR Report for the project and review it
with IDA not later than December 31, 2000 (para 4.10).
6.13    Land Acquisition and Resettlement: WAPDA and Provinces would ensure that all land
acquisition and involuntary displacement, and the subsequent resettlement and rehabilitation associated
with interventions of the project, are implemented in accordance with the FLAR. which has already been
agreed among the Borrower, Provinces and IDA (para 4.15).
6.14   Environmental Assessment: WAPDA  and Provinces would ensure that: (i) an Initial
Environmental Scoping (IES) is carried out for all Investment Projects; and (ii) full ElAs are prepared, to
the satisfaction of IDA, for all Investment Projects whose IES indicate that they would have significant
environmental impacts (para 4.16).
6.15   Environmental Management Plan (EMP): WAPDA and Provinces would implement the EMP
for the project as a whole dealing with the cumulative basin-wide environmental aspects and implications;
and environmental mitigation or enhancement measures indicated in the EIAs for individual Investment
Projects, to the satisfaction of IDA (para 4.17).
6.16   Environmental Monitoring and Audit:  WAPDA and Provinces would: (i) appoint, by
December 31, 1997, WAPDA's Environmental Cell and the Provincial EPA respectively, or an
internationally recognized environmental specialist acceptable to IDA, as the Environmental Auditor for
their activities under the project during the period of implementation; (ii) cause the Environmental
Auditors to issue their independent "Annual Environmental Audit Report" no later than six months after
the close of each fiscal year beginning from FY97/98; (iii) publish a summary of important audit findings
and recommendations in the project's progress reports; and (iv) implement the recommendations of the
Environmental Audit Report (para 4.18).
6.17   Wetlands Management Plan: WAPDA and Provinces would: (a) take measures to ensure that in
constructing field drains, wetlands are adequately protected; and (b) provide maps and infornation on
reclaimed areas, including the land use pattern for reclaimed lands and the date of reclamation (para 4.19).
6.18   Environment and Social Design Consultants: WAPDA would engage environment and social
design consultants with qualifications and terms of reference satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998 (para
4.20).
6.19   Impact Evaluation Report: The Borrower would prepare the Impact Evaluation Report for the
project within three years of the project's Closing Date (para 5.24).
6.20   M&E Consultants: WAPDA would engage M&E Consultants with qualifications and terTns of
reference satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998 (para 5.25).
C. RECOMMENDATION
6.21    With the above assurances and agreements, the Project would be suitable for an IDA Credit of
SDR 198.6 million (US$285 million equivalent) on standard terms with 35 years maturity.

Page 1 of 9
SELECTION CRITERIA FOR INVESTMENT PROJECTS
1.     Introduction: This annex outlines the criteria for selection of Investment Projects. It provides: (i)
selection criteria for Investment Projects; (ii) sponsoring agencies; (iii) the Investment Project approval cycle; and
(iv) guidelines for screening Investment Projects - general guidelines, and guidelines at formulation, feasibility, and
selection stage.
SELECTION CRITERIA FOR INVESTMENT PROJECTS
2.     Except as IDA shall otherwise agree, all Investment Projects financed under the project would meet the
following selection criteria:
(a)    the Investment Project is included in the Three Year Rolling PSDP for the project agreed with
IDA for the three next following Fiscal Years of project implementation;
(b)    in case of main off-farm drains, the Investment Project is located in an area that has lost at least 30
percent of its installed drainage capacity, or does not have drainage facilities at all;
(c)    the Investment Project supports a 'basin concept' for providing drainage to the area and is or
would be connected to an outfall;
(d)    the ERR of the Investment Project is not less than 15 percent;
(e)    a social assessment has been carried out for the Investment Project, demonstrating that, to the
extent possible the Investment Project benefits small farmers, women, and poorest one-third of the
income strata of the members of the farming community, and demonstrates that beneficiaries are
willing to make the level of contributions for the Investment Project specified in the Participation
Agreement for that category of projects;
(f)    an Initial Environmental Scoping has been carried out for the Investment Project; and an
"Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA)" for the Investment Project has been prepared,
wherever necessary;
(g)    a "Resettlement Action Plan (RAP)" which is in line with the 'Framework for Land Acquisition
and Resettlement' for the project satisfactory to IDA has been prepared for the Investment Project,
wherever necessary;
(h)    the Investment Project does not involve draining of an area in which highly sodic soils cover more
than 15 percent of such area;
(i)    the Investment Project does not involve draining wetlands;
(j)    a plan demonstrating that irrigation supplies from groundwater and surface water for irrigation to
the Investment Project area are (or would be) adequate to generate the expected benefits, and the
operation of channels would be modified to follow crop water requirements as closely as possible
and to distribute the available water equitably, has been prepared;
(k)    the Investment Project would have a net positive environmental impact on rural areas, and, in
particular, it would not be located in an area where excess irrigation water supplies have caused
waterlogging, unless a plan has been prepared demonstrating that measures would be taken to
reduce excess irrigation water supplies;



48
ANNEX l.
Page 2 of 9
(I)    the total cost of the Investment Project is less than $30 million, or such amount as IDA may agree
in given case, on an exceptional basis'; and a financing plan has been prepared for the Investment
Project setting forth, inter alia, the terms and conditions of financing to be provided for it out of
the proceeds of the IDA Credit;
(m)    the Investment Project is ready for implementation with detailed designs and tender documents
already prepared;
(n)    satisfactory supervisory arrangements including appointment of independent consultants2, have
been made for the Investment Project;
(o)    the implementation period of the Investment Project is not more than three years;
(p)    the projected completion date of the Investment Project is no later than December 31, 2003;
(q)    a post-completion O&M  Plan has been prepared for the Investment Project, including
demonstrating that the O&M would be carried out through perfonnance contracts awarded to
private sector contractors;
(r)    a procurement plan including contract packaging, applicable procedures, and the scheduling of the
procurement process has been prepared for the Investment Project;
(s)    the Investment Project would be carried out by an Implementing Agency which is eligible for
funding under the project, and whose statute provides the implementing agency with jurisdiction
over the Investment Project. The operating jurisdiction of the various Participating Agencies
would be:
(i)    Farmer Organization (FO): (i) on-farm  drainage; and (ii) on-farm  irrigation upto
minor/distributary level;
(ii)    Area Water Board (AWB):  intra-provincial irrigation and drainage within its canal
command (other than on-farm drainage and irrigation);
(iii)    Provincial Irrigation and Drainage Authority (PIDA): (i) intra-provincial irrigation and
drainage outside canal commands; and (ii) intra-provincial irrigation and drainage within
canal commands in which AWBs have not been established (other than on-farm drainage
and irrigation). This would be an interim arrangement until AWBs have been established
in all canal commands; and
(iv)    WAPDA: Inter-provincial irrigation and drainage.
(t)    in case of Investment Projects estimated to cost more than the equivalent of US$5 million, the
Investment Project has been appraised by a independent Panell of Experts appointed in
consultation with IDA.
It is expected that the cost would exceed $30 million in the case of the following three proposed projects: Lower Indus
Right Bank Irrigation and Drainage Project, Dera Ghazi Khan Drainage and Irrigation Project, and Left Bank Outfall Drain
(Completion) Project
2      Commensurate with the size of the project.

SPONSORING AGENCIES
3.     As indicated in para 2(s) above, Investment Projects would be eligible for financing under the project only
if they are carried out/sponsored by PAs which have the jurisdiction over the category of Investment Projects. PAs
would also carry out Investment Projects for which they have been contracted by any other PA (with operational
jurisdiction over the Investment Project) under the terms of a 'Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreement'
satisfactory to IDA. In particular:
(a)    WAPDA's Water Wing would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(i)    of an inter-Provincial nature;
(ii)    an integral part of LBOD or RBOD;
(iii)   contracted under a "Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreement" with a client on
terms satisfactory to IDA; and
(iv)    estimated to cost no less than $5 million equivalent.
(b)    PIDAs would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(i)    for the purpose of improving the PIDAs' ability to obtain or receive water from barrages
for delivery to AWBs at canal headworks;
(ii)   for the purpose of improving the PIDAs' ability to obtain or receive drainage effluent
from AWBs at outfalls for delivery to inter-Provincial drains or outfalls maintained and
operated by WAPDA's Water Wing;
(iii)   part of the PIDAs' paid responsibility on behalf of the Province for flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(iv)    contracted under a "Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreement" with a client on
terms satisfactory to IDA; and
(v)    estimated to cost no less than $3 million equivalent.
(c)    AWBs would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(i)    for the purpose of improving the AWBs' ability to obtain or receive water from canal
headworks operated by PIDAs for delivery to FOs at distributaries or minors;
(ii)    for the purpose of improving the AWBs' ability to obtain or receive drainage effluent
from FOs at outfalls operated by AWBs for delivery by the AWBs to inter-Provincial
drains or outfalls maintained and operated by PIDAs;
(iii)   part of the AWBs' paid responsibility on behalf of the PIDA for flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(iv)    contracted under a "Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreement" with that client
on terms satisfactory to IDA; and
(v)    estimated to cost no less than $1.0 million equivalent.
(d)    FOs would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(i)    for the purpose of improving FOs' ability to obtain or receive water from distributaries or
minors for delivery to Water Users Associations (WUAs) at minors or watercourses;
(ii)    for the purpose of improving the FOs' ability to obtain or receive drainage effluent from
WUAs or Drainage Beneficiary Groups (DBGs) at outfalls for delivery to drains or
outfalls maintained and operated by AWBs;
(iii)   part of the FOs' paid responsibility on behalf of the AWBs for flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(iv)    contracted under a "Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreement" with clients on
terms satisfactory to IDA;
(v)    for replacement of saline SCARP tubewells with tile drains;



50                                      ANNEX 1
Page 4 of 9
(vi)   for replacement of FGW SCARP tubewells with community tubewells;
(vii)  for improvements of watercourses in saline groundwater areas; and
(viii)  estimated to cost no less than $0.1 million equivalent.
THE INVESTMENT PROJECT APPROVAL CYCLE
4.     A feasibility report would be prepared for each Investment Project and endorsed by NDP Engineering
Design and Supervision Consultants. The Feasibility Reports would confirm and document that the Investment
Projects meet the selection criteria outlined in paragraphs 2 and 3 above.
5.     IDA would formally approve all Investment Projects that have estimated costs of $5 million or more,
regardless of the source of financing, subsequent to their appraisal by an Independent Panel of Experts. All other
Investment Projects would be approved by the NDP Coordination Cell or Provincial NDP Cell, and reviewed by
IDA retroactively. Investment Projects so reviewed which do not meet eligibility criteria would be ineligible for
financing.
6.     To ensure that IDA is consulted at early stages of the preparation process, rather than at a late stage, for
large projects or for projects with long preparation lead time, PAs would be encouraged to obtain IDA's approval on
a progressive basis, i.e., after each stage of the preparation process has been completed, for example:
formulation/identification; preparation of detailed Feasibility Study Report; appraisal by the NDP Engineering
Design and Supervision Consultants;); receipt of "no objection" of other interested parties (i.e. stakeholders)
including cofinanciers; signature of "Construction, Partnership and Handover Agreernent" between the PA and the
contracted agency (if any); preparation of detailed designs and tender documents of the designs; completion of land
acquisition, RAP, EIA, Social Assessment and other requirements; and completion of procurement procedures
including tender awards.
GUIDELINES FOR SCREENING INVESTMENT PROJECTS
7.     General Guidelines: All Investment Projects funded under NDP would meet criteria to ensure that
drainage schemes are sustainable, have positive returns to the national economy, have no significant negative
environmental impacts, have minimum financial burden on the Government, and involve beneficiary participation
and consultation during the entire Investment Project cycle. Detailed technical criteria for identification, ranking,
and selection are given in Annexes D and N of the Feasibility Report. As a general rule, before any Investment
Project is submitted for screening and selection for funding, in addition to traditional technical and economic
Investment Project feasibility considerations, the following eligibility criteria would ideally be met:
(a)    beneficiary participation and consultation plan in case of tertiary drainage or private tile drainage
Investment Projects;
(b)    Environmental Assessment with mitigation measures incorporated into Investment Project design;
(c)    Resettlement Action Plan with social rehabilitation dimensions;
(d)    adequate provision and budget for post-completion operations and maintenance;
(e)    community ownership and cost-sharing arrangements;
(f)    basin strategy;
(g)    hand-over arrangements, where applicable; and
(h)    awareness campaign directed at beneficiaries.
8.     Guidelines for Screening at Formulation Stage: The Investment Projects would be formulated by any
interested party or sponsor such as the Federal, Provincial or Local government bodies, farmers or other beneficiary
groups, or NGOs. The Investment Projects would be consistent with NDP objectives and be located in areas where
there are significant adverse conditions resulting from stormwater runoff, high watertable or soil salinity. In
addition, preference would be given to Investment Projects located in those areas where there are sufficient
resources, including irrigated water, an established Area Water Board, and organizations of farmers, that would
allow the benefits from drainage to be realized. At the Investment Project formulation stage, priority would ideally
be given to drainage requiring drainage with the following characteristics:



51
ANNEX 1
Page 5 of 9
(a)    located in highly developed irrigated zones with potentially high "gross margins," i.e., zones with
high cropping intensity, high yields, and cash crops; and
(b)    where over a 3-5 year period, the yields have been static or decreasing, the total cropped area is
falling, and farmers are shifting to cropping patterns that have lower returns.
9.     At the formulation stage, every effort would ideally be made to exclude any Investment Projects:
(a)    that do not have effective outfall to the main drainage system;
(b)    that require reclamation of highly sodic soils;
(c)    in abandoned areas, especially when cropping intensity in other areas not as severely affected can
be increased and irrigation water is scarce;
(d)    where salts would be mobilized from groundwater without adequate drainage outlet for safe
disposal;
(e)    that would have serious environmental impacts or problems which cannot easily be mitigated by
measures included within the project definition; and
(f)    that do not have a plan and budget for an awareness campaign concerning the benefits of drainage
and improved water management directed at beneficiaries.
10.    Guidelines for Screening at Feasibility Stage: In a situation where the number of candidate Investment
Projects is too large to allow all of them to be taken forward to the feasibility analysis stage, the following criteria
would be used for prioritizing Investment Project candidates:
(a)    Main off-farm drains: Only those that have lost at least 30 percent of their carrying capacity
would be included. Priority would normally be given based on the following criteria in
descending order:
(i)    where farmers are willing to rehabilitate subdrains on self-help basis and undertake
subsequent O&M;
(ii)    waterlogged area in a highly developed irrigated zone;
(iii)   stormwater drains in cotton-wheat zone; and
(iv)    other irrigated areas.
(b)    On-farm drains: All existing and new tributary drains with outfalls discharge less than 15 cusecs
would be given priority if they are to be rehabilitated or constructed under a community tertiary
drainage scheme or private tile drainage scheme. In this subcategory, priority would ideally be
given to (in descending order):
(i)    those Investment Projects with existing environmentally acceptable outfalls;
(ii)    areas underlain by saline groundwater (SGW) (for subsurface drainage); and
(iii)    Fresh groundwater (FGW) areas with poor aquifer.
(c)    Drainage tubewells (SGW): Reduction in discharge and specific capacity should ideally be
taken into account. SGW tubewell replacement and rehabilitation would only be considered if tile
drainage is not technically feasible; and if there is an environmental acceptable disposal
arrangement.
11.    Economic Analysis: All Investment Projects that pass feasibility stage would be subject to a detailed
economic analysis before consideration for funding under NDP. The analysis would closely follow the Planning
Commission's revised Guidelines dated October 1995 for preparing projects in the water sector (which include
social, environmental, hand-over, land acquisition and resettlement, and post-completion O&M aspects). To be
considered for funding under NDP, an Investment Project should have an economic rate of return (ERR) of at least
15%3 and a positive benefit/investment ratio.
3      The Opportunity Cost of Capital in Pakistan is estimated to lie somewhere between 12-15 %.



52
ANNEX 1
Page 6 of 9
12.    The guidelines are summarized in Table 1. A drainage technology selection flowchart is given in Figure 1.
The environmental evaluation procedures are given in Figure 2.
13.    The NDP Information System would be used to support analysis of the Investment Projects. In particular
Cost Tables, Indus Basin Model Revised (IBMR)4, and the geographical information system would be used to check
the validity and consistency of cost and benefit estimates, descriptions of the project area and affected lands, and
identification and assessment of environmental impacts. The Plan Generator component of the NDP Informaticn
System would also be used to simulate an objective comparison of the worth of altermative Investment Projects to
derive plans which are optimal within the assumed budgetary constraints.
14.    Least-Cost Slice-and-Package Investment Projects: To ease the administrative burden and expedite
approval, Investment Projects whose costs are estimated by the sponsors and confirmed by the NDP Coordination
Cell or Provincial NDP Cell to cost below $10 million would be implemented on the basis of least-cost slice-and-
package procedures under which standard costs and other uniformly applicable criteria would be applied to the
evaluation, financing, and implementation of the Investment Projects. Such procedures would be developed for all
categories of Investment Projects, but are expected to be applied most frequently for on-farm drainage; lining of
watercourses in SGW areas; transition of FGW tubewells; transfer, rehabilitation or construction of subdrains;
installation of standard measurement, gauging and control equipment; O&M Performance Contracts; repetitive
consultancy packages for identical services or clients; repetitive equipment and machinery for identical clients or
purposes; training; and for eligible procurement and expenditures of AWBs, FOs, NGOs, WUAs, DBGs, and
community organizations. The NDP Coordination Cell, working in coordination with Provincial NDP Cells, wou].d
submit and agree with IDA annually: (i) the package of Investment Projects; and (ii) standard guidelines and unit
rates for implementation of projects under the Least-Cost Slice-and-Package approach.
4       To support the economic analysis, IBMR would be used in a revised form to simulate the direct and indirect impacts of
the investment project on the cropping pattem, resource use, farmers' income, and labor requirements vis-a-vis changes in
salinity and watertable. The revised version of IBMR would include upgrading and validation of the IBMR at the micro
(project) level to represent the impacts of individual investment projects within an agro-climatic zone, including more accurate
agricultural production data, yield-salinity and yield-watertable coefficients, and land use and cropping decisions. The model
would also be further refined to model lateral flows and evaporation.

TABLE 1: GUIDELINES FOR SCHEME FORMULATION
Physical Characteristics:
Stormwater and Rice Drainage:
*  Work on existing:
(a) main/branch drains & their structures, to prevent frequent damage to crops and/or
infrastructure;
(b) structures on tributary drains if beneficiaries do earthworks and subsequent maintenance.
*  New Drains to:
(a) remove excess irrigation water for timely sowing of rabi crop after rice;
(b) reduce identifiable production losses due to rainstorms in Cotton-Wheat Zones;
(c) reduce frequent quantifiable rainstorm damage to crops and infrastructure in highly
developed areas;
(d) on-farm drains in small waterlogged pockets of irrigated areas provided an outfall is
available, beneficiaries are small landowners, share cost of construction and undertake
responsibility of O&M.
Subsurface drainage:
* augmentation, rehabilitation or replacement of existing or develop new subsurface drainage facility
in non-rice areas with Depth to Watertable (DWT) < 0.9m all year for several years; surface drains
and water management actions have failed to provide relief provided;
(a) areas in the SGW zone; or FGW zone where aquifer characteristics are not conducive to
private tubewell development;
(b) environmentally acceptable outfall is available;
(c) on-farm drainage of small waterlogged pockets of irrigated areas provided an outfall is
available, beneficiaries are small land owner, share cost of construction and undertake
responsibility of O&M.
Environmental Mitigation:
* improve environmental performance of existing surface and subsurface drainage projects in SGW
pockets by providing:
(a) environmentally acceptable outfall;
(b) altemate mode of subsurface drainage when the replacement of existing facilities become
due.
Agricultural Characteristics:
* drainage-deficient areas where, over at least 3 to 5 years, yields have been static or falling, cropped
areas have been falling, and/or farmers have been changing to lower-return crops.

PARTICIPATION AGREEMENT
ASPECTS TO BE COVERED IN PARTICIPATION AGREEMENTS
1. Introduction: This Annex sets out the aspects which would be covered in Participation Agreements
between Provinces and PIDAs, AWBs and FOs participating in the Project. The Participation Agreements
would be between the concemed Province and the PIDA, AWB or FO to which funds from the Project are
being provided by the Province concerned. A separate Participation Agreement would be signed with each
PIDA, AWB or FO. Legal Counsel financed under the Project, or NDP Consultants would provide
assistance required by the Provinces, PIDAs, AWBs, or FOs in preparing and negotiating the Participation
Agreement on request by the Province/PIDA, AWB or FO.
2. Effectiveness: The Participation Agreement would become effective upon the date of its signature or
on the Effective Date of the Development Credit Agreement and Project Agreement for NDP, whichever is
later.
3. Compliance with Other Agreements: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would comply with the
provisions of all relevant sections of the Development Credit Agreement and Project Agreement for the
project signed with IDA, and with similar agreements with ADB and OECF for the project.
4. Eligibility for Incremental Financing Commitments: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned shall
furnish with respect to each Fiscal Year of Project implementation, evidence to IDA, showing that they are,
and shall continue during such Fiscal Year to be, in compliance with the eligibility criteria set forth in
Schedule 1 to the Project Agreement (these eligibility criteria are outlined in Annex 6 of the SAR). The
PIDA, AWB or FO would be eligible for incremental financing commitments from the IDA Credit for new
programs of activities to be commenced under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for
on-going Investment Projects only after it has furnished this evidence.
5. Organization and Functions: The PIDA, AWBs or FO would: (i) maintain organizational structure,
functions, staffing, and regulatory framework, all satisfactory to IDA, for the period of project
implementation and post-completion monitoring; and (ii) promptly inform IDA of any proposed change in
the organizational structures, functions, staffing, or regulatory framework.
6. Autonomy, Accountability, and Efficiency: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would be: (i)
established and run as an autonomous entity; (ii) established and run in accordance with generally accepted
business practice, under which Owners (whether Provinces or farmers), Board of Directors, and
Management would be completely separate; and (iii) audited by Chartered Accountants appointed in
consultation with IDA.
7. Recruitment of Managing Directors and Senior Officers of PIDAs, AWBs and FOs: The PIDA or
AWB concerned would recruit Managing Directors and Senior Officers from PIDs and/or the market
through transparent processes (i.e., including by advertising in the press, and the use of specialized
professional management recruitment firms). Managing Directors and Senior Officers would be acceptable
to IDA.
8. Staffing Levels: The PIDA or AWB concerned would prepare and implement a "Staffng,
Operational and Financial Plan"; impose a hiring freeze; reassign staff; and encourage voluntary retirement
until it achieves the desired staffing levels.
9. Regulatory and Corporate Oversight: The PIDA concerned would: (i) establish a Policy &
Regulation Wing; and (ii) assign responsibility for establishing policy and regulating the operations of
entities to the Wing.



64                                    ANNEX 3
Page 2 of 7
10. Legal Cell: The PIDA concerned would establish a Legal Cell with Tenns of Reference and staff,
including Chief Legal Counsel/Officer, agreed with IDA, to advise on regulatory and legal matters relating
to the decentralized irrigation and drainage system.
Operations
11. Management Transfer: The management of the irrigation and drainage system in the operating
jurisdiction of the PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would be legally transferred to it through leases or other
contractually enforceable mechanism which shall have been established by the Province in consultation
with IDA. The operating jurisdiction of the PIDA, AWB or FO would be as given below:
(a)    FO: (i) on-farm drainage; and (ii) on-farn irrigation upto minor/distributary level;
(b)    AWB: intra-provincial irrigation and drainage within its canal command (other than on-
farm drainage and irrigation); and
(c)    PIDA: (i) intra-provincial irrigation and drainage outside canal commands; and (ii) intra-
provincial irrigation and drainage within canal commands in which AWBs have not been
established (other than on-farm drainage and irrigation). This would be an interim
arrangement until AWBs have been established in all canal comamands.
12. Service Standards: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would adhere to a clear set of service
standards which shall have been agreed with its clients, and which shall be monitorable and contractually
enforceable.
13. Streamlining and Cost Reduction in Operations of Decentralized Irrigation Institutions: The
PIDA, AWB, or FO concerned would implement measures aimed at reducing O&M costs, and thereby
reduce the cost recovery base including: (a) formulating new service regulations and personnel policies; (b)
streamlining machine operations; (c) updating and revising service and technical manuals; (d) improving
accounting and financial management systems; (e) conducting specific diagnostic analyses and
implementing subsequent action plans to streamline operations of selected drainage circles; (f) streamlining
fmancing and utilization of the O&M budget - inter alia by linking O&M financing with collection of
Abiana (the financing aspect of streamlining) and increasing the share of works in the budget (the
utilization aspect of streamlining) in selected pilot areas; (g) streamlining implementation of off-farm
drainage O&M through Performance Contracts (PCs) or Rehabilitate and Operate Contracts (ROCs) or
other scheme awarded to the private sector on competitive basis, and designating Drainage Circles for PCs;
(h) initiating pilots to test decentralization of Abiana assessment and collection during implementation of
NDP, and designating Circles where pilots to test decentralization of Abiana assessment and
implementation would be implemented; (i) rationalizing "Abiana" schedule; (j) building their capacities for
delivery of services under the new framework; (k) transferring on-farm drains and tertiary drains to FOs
and WUAs; and (I) transitioning as many FGW tubewells as possible.
14. Delivery and Pricing for Wholesale Irrigation and Drainage Services: The PIDA, AWB, or FO
concerned would design, test/pilot, and if successful, implement a system of demand, delivery, and
payment of wholesale irrigation and drainage services all based on advance planning prior to the
agricultural seasons. Under such a system, PIDAs would eventually deliver services to AWBs based on the
aggregate demand from them, while AWBs would do likewise based on aggregate demand from FOs, who
would base theirs on the demand from WUAs. Payment would be determined through negotiations at these
aggregate levels as well; and losses (arising from operational inefficiencies arising from mismanagement
and/or overstaffing, non-recovery of charges, leakages due to corruption, or system losses due to excessive
seepage or poor maintenance) would be absorbed by the responsible parties, and not transmitted system-
wide. PIDAs would have the power to set water charges to AWBs only; aind would sell wholesale
irrigation and drainage services to them on a full cost-recovery basis. PIDAs' receivables from individual
AWBs would be independent of AWBs' receipts from FOs; and losses would not be transferred from one



65                                             ANNEX 3
Page 3 of 7
AWB to another. PIDAs would compensate AWBs for services for which AWBs are not expected to
recover costs; or which they carry out at the behest or direction of PIDAs. AWBs would similarly set
wholesale charges and deliver services to, and obtain payment from, individual FOs; and FOs would do so
likewise with WUAs.
15. Operating Regulations: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would prepare, jointly with all the other
PAs, Operating Regulations and Manual of Procedures for the Project. The Operating Regulations and
Manual of Procedures would specify the general principles, terms and conditions for financing under the
project, roles and responsibilities of each PA, procedures for Investment Project preparation and selection,
eligibility criteria for PAs, eligible expenditures for financing, and a glossary of terms.
16. Operational Manuals and Procedures: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would develop detailed
Operational Manuals and Procedures in consultation with the NDP Design and Engineering Supervision
Consultants for each Investment Project; and submit them to IDA no later than one year prior to
completion of the Investment Project.
17. O&M Performance Contracts: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would award at least one multi-
year O&M Performance Contract in each year for maintenance of O&M facilities. Small AWBs and FOs
may be exempted from the requirement to award more than one such contract.
18. Capacity Utilization: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would achieve average annual capacity
utilization rates for irrigation and drainage machinery and equipment of at least 60 percent in the first year
of operation, 70 percent in the second year, and 80 percent in the third year and beyond of its participation
in the project as separate entities.
19. Collection Ratio: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would achieve a minimum collection ratio on all
receivables (including Abiana and Drainage Cess) of not less than 60 percent in the first year of operation,
75 percent in the second year, and 90 percent in the third year and thereafter.
20. Budget: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would allocate not less than 60 percent of its non-
recurrent budget to non-staff expenses in the first year of operation, 70 percent in the second year, and 80
percent in the third year and thereafter.
21. Water Allocation Committees: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would establish, a "Water
Allocation Committee, or WAC" for each point of off-take (i.e., from barrages to canal headworks, from
headworks to distributaries, and from distributaries to watercourses) to improve the transparency of
allocation of irrigation supplies. The WACs would publish annually or more regularly in the local press
and in the Provinces' or Districts' official gazette the allocations of irrigation supplies, with comparisons of
rated/authorized versus actual allocations.
22. Public Participation: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would establish Community Advisory
Committees (CACs) on various issues which require the local knowledge, advisory inputs and active
participation of NGOs, farmers' associations, local community leaders and other stakeholders to help them
manage better the interface of the project with impacted communities including, but not limited to, land
acquisition, environment, protection of local wetland resources and similar interventions which may be
important to the livelihoods of local communities. The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would hold at least
one consultative and informative public meeting in March before the formulation of the year's work
program and budget; and during the middle of the fiscal year to brief the stakeholders about the progress in
implementing the year's work program and budget.
23. Procurement: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would follow the World Bank's procurement
guidelines and standard bidding documents for procurement of all works, goods and services which would
be funded by IDA under the Project; and the ADB's and OECF's procurement guidelines for procurement



66                                      ANNEX 3
Page 4 of 7
of all works, goods and services which would be funded by the ADB and OECF respectively under the
Project.
Institutional Program
24. The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would submit a work program and specific proposals for various
aspects of its institutional program which would be funded under the project. These would be submitted as
part of the Business Plan (see para 30 below).
Investment Projects
25. The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would use the funds provided under the project for Investment
Projects to implement Investment Projects which are approved under the selection procedures agreed under
the project and which meet selection criteria specified in the Project Agreement.
26. A PIDA would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(a)    for the purpose of improving the PIDA's ability to obtain or receive water from barrages
for delivery to AWBs at canal headworks;
(b)    for the purpose of improving the PIDA's ability to obtain or receive drainage effluent
from AWBs at outfalls for delivery to inter-Provincial drains or outfalls maintained and
operated by WAPDA's Water Wing;
(c)    part of the PIDA's paid responsibility on behalf of the Province for flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(d)    contracted under a "Construction Partnership and Handover Agreement" with a client on
terms satisfactory to IDA; and
(e)    estimated to cost no less than $3 million equivalent.
27. An AWB would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(a)    for the purpose of improving the AWB's ability to obtain or receive water from canal
headworks operated by a PIDA for delivery to FOs at distributaries or minors;
(b)    for the purpose of improving the AWB's ability to obtain or receive drainage effluent
from FOs at outfalls operated by the AWB for delivery by the AWB to inter-Provincial
drains or outfalls maintained and operated by a PIDA;                  I
(c)    part of the AWB's paid responsibility on behalf of a PIDA ior flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(d)    contracted under a "Construction Partnership and Handover Agreement" with a client on
terms satisfactory to IDA; and
(e)    estimated to cost no less than $1.0 million equivalent.
28. A FO would ideally sponsor Investment Projects that are:
(a)    for the purpose of improving the FO's ability to obtain or receive water from
distributaries or minors for delivery to WUAs at minors or watercourses;
(b)    for the purpose of improving the FO's ability to obtain or rece:ive drainage effluent from
WUAs at outfalls for delivery to drains or outfalls maintained and operated by an AWB;
(c)    part of the FOs' paid responsibility on behalf of an AWB for flood control or flood
damage rehabilitation;
(d)    contracted under a "Construction Partnership and Handover Agreement' with clients on
terms satisfactory to IDA;
(e)    replacement of saline SCARP tubewells with tile drains;
(f)    replacement of FGW SCARP tubewells with community tubewells;



67                                       ANNEX3
Page 5 of 7
(g)     improvements of watercourses; and
(h)     estimated to cost no less than $0.1 million equivalent.
29. Construction Partnership and Hand-Over Agreement: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned may
engage WAPDA, another PIDA, AWB or FO or firm to construct irrigation and drainage facilities on its
behalf. This would be based on a 'Construction Partnership and Hand-Over Agreements', which would be
for specific works, and would ideally specify: (i) terms and conditions; (ii) roles and responsibilities of
each party to the contract; (iii) detailed procedures for hand-over of completed works from these agencies
to the PIDA, AWB or FO concerned; and (iv) financial obligations, sureties, guarantees, penalties and
default clauses. Such agreements would contain provisions for enforceable performance bonds of value
equal to at least 10 percent of the value of the contract to be issued by each contracting party to the other at
the time of signature.
Business Plans, Finances and Budgets
30.    Business Plans: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would prepare, revise and agree annually a
Three Year Rolling Business Plan with the Province on or before March 31 of each year, which would
include procurement, staffing, operations, and financing plans/projections. The Plan shall demonstrate
that: (a) in case of a PIDA and an AWB, that the PIDA and AWB shall be financially self-sustainable for
O&M costs', within ten years of its establishment; and (b) in case of an FO, that the FO shall be financially
self-sustainable2 within seven years of its establishment.
31. General Manager-Finance: The PIDA or AWB concerned would appoint a professionally qualified
accountant (i.e., Chartered Accountant or Cost Accountant) as General Manager-Finance.
32. Accounts and Audit: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would prepare financial statements in
accordance with Accounting Standards of the Pakistan Institute of Chartered Accountants, would follow
the Fiscal Year (July to June) as its accounting year, and would maintain books of accounting on
commercially-oriented basis (as opposed to government accounting). The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned
would appoint a firm/firm(s) of Chartered Accountants as auditors before it becomes eligible to participate
in the project. The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would not be eligible for funds from all project sources
(i.e. the Borrower, Provinces, IDA and other donors) if it fails to submit its audited accounts for the
previous Fiscal Year by December 31.
Social and Environmental Aspects
33. Land Acquisition and Resettlement: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would implement all land
acquisition and involuntary displacement, and the subsequent resettlement and rehabilitation associated
with interventions of the project, in accordance with the Framework for Land Acquisition and Resettlement
which has been agreed among the Borrower, Provinces and IDA.
34. Environmental Impact Assessments: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would ensure that: (a) an
Initial Environmental Scoping (IES) is conducted for all Investment Projects; and (b) all Investment
I      Generation of sufficient income from all sources and beneficiaries to meet O&M costs, operating costs, de-
preciation of assets, and payments for irrigation and drainage services (to upper-tier organizations, e.g.: in case of an
AWB, the upper-tier entity would be a PIDA).
2       Financial self-sustainability shall be defined as generation of: (i) sufficient income from all sources and
beneficiaries to meet its O&M costs, operating costs, depreciation of assets, and payments for irrigation and drainage
services (to upper-tier organizations, e.g.: in case of an FO, the upper-tier entity would be an AWB), and debt service
payments; and (ii) sufficient funds from its own resources and/or from borrowings to meet capital expenditure re-
quirements.



68                                    ANNEX 3
Page 6 of 7
Projects whose IES indicate that they would have significant environmental impacts would undergo
complete Environmental Impact Assessments (ELAs).
35. Field Draihs: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would: (a) take measures to ensure that in
constructing field drains, wetlands are adequately protected; and (b) provide maps and information on
reclaimed areas, including the land use pattern for reclaimed lands and the date of reclamation.
36. Draining of Riverine Areas: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would ensure that any proposal to
drain the Sindh Riverine areas, areas between the main drains and the coast, flood plains, or lake shores,
would be subject to full EIAs, in accordance with Pakistan's environmental protection laws and Bank
policy, prior to approval.
Other Aspects
37. Evaluation Reports: Consultants from the NDP Cell in WAPDA would provide technical assistance
to the PIDA, AWB or FO concerned as required on request by the PIDA, AWB or FO on the basis of a
Service Contract. The Chief Executive of the PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would complete one or more
Evaluation Reports (based on standardized formats) during and after the completion of each such Service
Contract.
38. Information Disclosure: The PIDA, AWB or FO concerned would subscribe to the project's policy
and standards in favor of a high degree of public participation and disclosure of project information to the
public and the stakeholders in particular i.e., a general requirement would exist in favor of public
disclosure and widespread dissemination of all of the project's formal/official reports, through publication
of summary leaflets and paid advertisements in local newspapers with translations in the local languages.
The only exception would be for project-related correspondence and for those documents which are
formally designated as being restricted in circulation, by agreement between the Borrower, the Provinces
and the IDA, OECF, and ADB.
39. Notices: Any notice or request required or permitted to be given or made under the Agreement would
be in writing and would be deemed to have been duly given or made when it shall be delivered to the
Province. Any action required or permitted, or any documents required or permitted, to be executed under
the Agreement on behalf of the PIDA, AWB or FO would be taken or executed by its duly authorized
representatives or such persons as it shall designate in writing.
Provision of Funds by Provinces
40. The Province would provide funds as a grant to the PIDA, AWB or FO concerned equal to the cost of
the Investment Project/institutional program minus the share of cost to be shared by the beneficiaries as an
upfront contribution, as detailed in the table below. These funds which the Provinces would provide would
comprise funds provided by Donors and the Province's counterpart funds.
