PROCUREMENT ARRANGEMENTS
INTRODUCTION
1.     Procurement Assessment: The Borrower and IDA have carried out a "Country Procurement
Assessment for Pakistan" in 1995; and the Report is expected to be published soon. The Assessment
Mission concluded that the procurement policies and practices of all the major Executing Agencies for the
project (including WAPDA and Provinces) need to be brought into compliance with IDA procurement
policies; but that the Borrower and WAPDA in particular had the potential to implement these policies
satisfactorily. A number of changes have been agreed to be made to the procurement documentation of the
Borrower and WAPDA, which would bring them in compliance with IDA's requirements.
2.     The NDP Procurement Unit: WAPDA would establish an NDP Procurement Unit with terms of
reference, staffing from WAPDA and procurement consultants, and budgets satisfactory to IDA. WAPDA
would appoint one or more consultants with internationally recognized professional qualifications in
procurement administration, from NDP Engineering Design and Supervision Consultants or other
consultants, as NDP Procurement Advisers to provide technical assistance and training to staff of WAPDA,
PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs on procurement. An NDP Procurement Manager (PM) will head the NDP
Procurement Unit which will be established by the NDP Cell. The PM will be the Deputy Chief Resident
Engineer (Contracts) of the NDP Engineering Design and Supervision Consultants. The PM will develop
policies and procedures for the Procurement Unit, train the staff and promote effective use of the Credit
for project expenditures by Participating Agencies (PAs). To ensure consistency and quality in the
application of agreed procurement standards and procedures, the PM will prepare or endorse all
procurement documents by PAs before they are submitted to IDA. The overall responsibility for
procurement under the project will be with the NDP PM and his Regional Deputy PMs (DPMs). The PM
will manage procurement and other aspects of the project in a highly decentralized manner. The NDP
Procurement Unit, through its Regional Offices, would endorse procurement recommendations of PA line
managers to IDA for its no objection, before contracts are awarded.
3.     The Borrower's Procurement Review Arrangements: The Appraisal Mission concluded that
the Borrower, WAPDA, prospective PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs would be capable of handling procurement,
supervising contract administration, and engaging and supervising consultants envisaged under NDP with
the help of procurement consultants and establishment of the NDP Procurement Unit. WAPDA, Provinces,
and PAs would significantly delegate and decentralize the responsibility and authority for approval of
procurement decisions. For example, the representatives of the PA concerned with procurement (e.g.
Central Contracts Cell in the case of WAPDA), of the PAs' line manager (e.g. concerned General Manager
in the case of WAPDA or Chief Engineer in the case of PIDAs and AWBs), and a representative of the
NDP Coordinator, would be represented at the decision meeting at which the Procurement Committee
would make the recommendation for award, prior to its submission to IDA. The Procurement Committee
would be required to convey its decisions regarding procurement brought to it within a specific period.
Since approval of contracts by the WAPDA Authority (equivalent of Board) is the primary cause of delays
in procurement in projects implemented by WAPDA, WAPDA would: (i) delegate final approval authority
for all procurement for civil works contracts below $20 million, goods contracts below $10 million, and
consultancy contracts below $10 million which are frnanced under the project and implemented by
WAPDA to a "NDP Procurement Review Sub-committee" of the Authority established under the
respective General Manager, and with representation from the NDP Procurement Unit. The Central
Contracts Cell (CCC) of WAPDA would be represented on the subcommittee. All contracts above these
thresholds which will be implemented by WAPDA would be referred to the WAPDA Authority (equivalent
of Board); and (ii) delegate powers to the NDP Program Coordinator to approve up to 80 percent of the
procurement values which are expected to require WAPDA's approval under the project'. Authority for
I      Since Negotiations, WAPDA has proposed the following alternative arrangement: "WAPDA in consultation
with IDA, would: (i) establish an NDP Procurement Unit with staffing from WAPDA, Procurement Consultants and
Finance; (ii) appoint a Consultant with internationally recognized professional qualification in procurement



71                                       ANNEX 4
Page 2 of 6
approving procurement decisions for contracts implemented by PIDAs and AWBs would rest with the
Engineer. IDA's Guidelines for Procurement under IDA Credits would be followed for procurement of all
works and goods financed from the Credit. Consultants financed from the Credit would be selected
following IDA's Guidelines for Selection and Use of Consultants.
4.     Standard Bidding Documents (SBDs): Standard Bidding Documents (SBDs) jointly prepared by
IDA, the Borrower, and WAPDA for Pakistan will be completed and approved by both IDA and the
Borrower by the time this project becomes ready for implementation. IDA and the Borrower have agreed
that the SBDs would be used for all procurement of works, goods and consultants financed by the IDA
Credit. Pending the issuance of SBDs, all procurement which is processed prior to that date would be on
the basis of existing IDA SBDs.
WORKS
5.     Procurement Method: All IDA-financed contracts estimated to cost the equivalent of $5 million
or more would be procured using ICB procedures. Based on the currently identified and/or agreed package
of prospective civil works expenditures under various Investment Projects, it is expected that IDA-financed
civil works contracts amounting to $123.1 million equivalent will be procured using ICB procedures.
These works comprise individually lumpy contracts including: (a) rehabilitation and remodeling of the
LBOD Spinal Drain ($30.6 million); (b) remedial works on the Tidal Link ($11.7 million); (c) installation
of electrical lines, in Sanghar and Mirpurkhas districts ($1.8 million); (d) construction of the Chotiari
Reservoir ($26.6 million); (e) remodeling of the Nara Canal (23.7 million; 3 contracts); (f) works on the
Jamrao Canal ($6.3 million); (g) installation of control and telecommunicatio:n equipment in the Nara
Canal Command Area ($4.2 million); (h) installation of tile drains in Mirpurkhas ($9.1 million); and (i)
construction and rehabilitation of drainage infrastructure ($9.1 million, 3 contracts). Qualified domestic
bidders competing under ICB will be eligible for a 7.5 percent preference in bid evaluation, in accordance
with IDA guidelines on procurement. IDA-financed contracts costing less than $5 million each would be
awarded under NCB procedures acceptable to IDA. The total estimated cost of such contracts is $66.6
million. These civil works comprise numerous packages of rehabilitation, small structures, earthworks and
operation and maintenance spread throughout the Indus Basin, and may be of limited interest to foreign
contractors. NCB has been used extensively for small civil works under all recent and ongoing irrigation
and drainage projects in Pakistan, and found to work satisfactorily under the right operating environment in
implementing agencies. However, there is much room for improvement in the procurement processing and
contract management practices and capacities of WAPDA and the PIDs (future PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs).
TIhe remaining IDA-financed civil works, mainly earthwork, masonry work, and[ small structures, will be
carried out by direct contracting, using project beneficiary labor (and/or materials) mobilized by FOs, with
progress payments based on unit prices agreed with IDA. While accurate estimates are currently not
available, these contracts are expected to aggregate $17.3 million equivalent.
6.     Procurement Review Thresholds: All pre-qualification documents and proposals would be
subject to IDA's prior review regardless of threshold. The following IDA-financed contracts would be
subject to IDA's prior review:
(a)    contracts for civil works estimated to cost more than $5 million equivalent;
(b)    the first NCB contract by each PA;
(c)    O&M Performance Contracts, turnkey and supply-and-erect contracts (e.g. for dredging
equipment); and
(d)    contracts for borderline services such as GIS, aerial and satellite mapping.
administration as NDP Procurement Adviser; and (iii) constitute an NDP Procurement Review Committee headed by
the Regional General Manager comprising the Project Consultants and the NDP Project M[anager or his representative
to carry out one step evaluation of procurement contracts including works, goods and consultancy, where applicable.
The report of this Committee will be reviewed by CCC before approval from Managing Director (Water) or the
Authority as the case may be".



72                                      ANNEX 4
Page 3 of 6
All IDA-financed contracts not subject to IDA's prior review would be subject to post review on a sample
basis.
7.     Procurement Documents: SBDs for Pakistan would be used after these are finalized by the
Borrower, WAPDA and IDA. Until these are finalized, IDA's SBDs for Procurement of Works would be
used for ICB contracts; and IDA's SBDs for Procurement of Works (Smaller Contracts) with modifications
agreed with IDA would be used for NCB contracts. Pre-qualification would be done using IDA's Standard
Pre-qualification Document for Works.
8.     Prequalification of Bidders for Works: Prequalification would be undertaken for all contracts
(or groups of contracts awarded on slice-and-package basis) estimated to cost $15 million or more.
Prequalification would be updated annually. Prequalification would be done using the IDA's Standard
Prequalification Documents for Works. Prequalification criteria would include financial strength, past
performance, availability of equipment and staff, and quality of the "method statement". The prequalified
contractor and supplier lists would be subject to IDA's "no objection", and only those prequalified would
be eligible to participate in the bidding. Where post-qualification is considered unavoidable, the same
criteria would be applied retrospectively in bid evaluation. All pre-qualification documents and proposals
would be subject to IDA's prior review regardless of threshold. The procurement process and
prequalification process have been initiated with the General Procurement Notice which was published in
April 1995.
GOODS
9.     Procurement Method: All IDA-financed contracts for goods costing $300,000 equivalent or
more would be procured using ICB procedures. These contracts would include steel, pumps, transformers,
generators, construction and O&M equipment and machinery, communication and monitoring equipment
with an estimated total cost of $15.9 million. Qualified domestic bidders competing under ICB would be
eligible for a 15 percent preference in bid evaluation, or custom duties and import taxes payable by a non-
exempt importer, whichever is less. The remainder, mostly vehicles, would be procured through NCB
(estimated total cost: $2.4 million), except those contracts costing less than $50,000 (mostly office
equipment) which would be procured using National Shopping procedures (estimated total cost: $0.4
million).
10.    Procurement Review Thresholds for Goods: The following IDA-financed contracts would be
subject to IDA's prior review:
(a)    contracts for goods and equipment estimated to cost $300,000 or more;
(b)    the first NCB contract by each PA; and
(c)    contracts for borderline services such as GIS, aerial and satellite mapping.
All IDA-financed contracts not subject to IDA's prior review would be subject to post review on sample
basis.
11.    Procurement Documents: SBDs for Pakistan would be used after these are finalized by the
Borrower, WAPDA and IDA. Until these are finalized, IDA's SBDs for Procurement of Goods would be
used for contracts awarded using ICB procedures.
12.    Documents To be Reviewed Under Prior Review: In case of contracts for goods and works
subject to prior review, each of the following stages and related documentation in the procurement process
would be reviewed and commented upon by IDA before they are implemented by the Borrower or PA: (a)
advertising procedures; (b) pre-qualification invitation documents, and subsequent evaluation; (c) bidding
documents and addenda; (d) bid evaluation and the proposal for contract award; (e) contract documents, to
identify any differences from the proforma contract included in the bidding documents and to verify



73                                      ANNEX4
Page 4 of 6
consistency with bid evaluation; and (f) material modifications to the contract during execution. Since the
project involves numerous procurements of similar goods, works, and services by all participating
agencies, most commercial documents would be common to similar items of procurement, and hence will
be reviewed once and then used repetitively. Only modifications to the standard document to suit specific
procurement, if any, would need to be submitted to IDA each time for prior review.
CONSULTANCY SERVICES
13.    The Services: IDA would finance the following consulting services: (i) NDP Design and
Engineering Supervision Consultants (about 8596 man-months); (ii) sector planning and policy studies
consultants; and (iii) financial management and information systems consultants; (iv) social design and
environmental consultants; (v) monitoring and evaluation consultants; and (vi) other individual long- and
short-term consultants e.g. for training, development communications, editorial specialists, panels of
experts, accounting and auditing, etc.
14.    Selection of Consultants: All consultants whose services are financed from the IDA Credit will
be selected by PAs in accordance with procedures outlined in "Guidelines for Use of Consultants by World
Bank Borrowers and by the World Bank as Executing Agency (August 1981) ". IDA's Standard Letter of
Invitation and Standard Form of Contract for Consultants' Services will be used for consultancy services.
15.    Prior Review: The following IDA-financed contracts would be subject to IDA's prior review:
(a)    consultancy contracts with firms with estimated cost of $100,000 or more, and with
individuals with estimated cost of $50,000 or more;
(b)    the first contract for appointment of consultants for each PA;
(c)    contracts with firms awarded on single-source basis; and
(d)    consultancy contracts for assignments of a critical nature (e.g., because of environmental,
safety, or public health considerations, Panels of Experts, Consultants for the Enhanced
Supervision Arrangements, Sector Planning and Research, Monitoring and Evaluation
including Environmental Monitoring and Audit, Social Assessments, Resettlement,
Environmental    Assessments,   Information     Systems,    and    Financial
Management/Accounting and Auditing), regardless of value.
Terms of reference for all IDA-financed consultancy contracts would also be subject to prior review,
regardless of value. All IDA-fnanced contracts which are not subject to prior review would be subject to
post review on sample basis.
16.    In case of consultancy contracts which are subject to IDA's prior review, the Borrower would
submit for IDA's review relevant documents at each stage of the process by which the Borrower selects
consulting fimns including: (a) preparation of terms of reference and budget; (b) choice of selection
procedure; (c) preparation of the shortlist; (d) Letter of Invitation; (e) submission of the winning proposal
or the evaluation report; and (f) negotiation of the draft contract.
17.    In view of their specialized capabilities, technology transfer and institutional/capacity building
experience, and good results from previous and ongoing technical cooperation services, WAPDA may
contract directly the services of agencies of some member countries to support its "Institutional Program
for WAPDA's Water Wing" subcornponent and to support its "Research Program" subcomponent. In
order to increase accountability of the research institutes carrying out the drainage research programs,
participating drainage research institutes would enter into contracts with WAPDA to carry out their
research programs with payments linked to defined outputs and maintenance of agreed standards and
criteria. It is expected that WAPDA would award about 13 such contracts ($12.9 million).
18.    In addition to the above provisions, the following would be reviewed by IDA (for goods, works,
and consultancy contracts):



74                                       ANNEX 4
Page 5 of 6
(a)    any case in which the procedures used are not transparent or award recommendation is
irregular;
(b)    any case in which a complaint has been raised;
(c)    any request for re-bidding;
(d)    standard procurement documents to be used under the project;
(e)    proposals for extension of bid validity, or delays in contract award;
(f)    all advance procurement action, advance contracting, and procurement relating to
retroactive financing for ICB and NCB contracts;
(g)    all contracts which are proposed to be awarded to entities, companies, or agencies which
are part of, owned or controlled by, the Borrower, its Provinces, WAPDA, or any other
PA; and
(h)    sole-source procurement contracts.
19.    Contracts Under Prior Review Threshold: Since only the indicative pipeline of Investment
Projects is known with any degree of firmness, the number of contracts which are likely to fall under the
prior review threshold cannot be determined at this stage, but is estimated to be about $123.1 million for
works (about 60% of IDA-financed contracts), $15.9 million for goods (85% of IDA-fmanced contracts),
$76.9 million for consultancy services (98% of IDA-fnanced contracts), and $14.2 million for research
contracts (100% of IDA-financed contracts). About 67% of all IDA-financed contracts would be covered
by prior review, which is below the desirable level of 80%, but is acceptable because it has been selected to
strike a balance between the work load for IDA on prior review and an acceptable coverage for IDA-
financed contracts in number and value, given the potentially large number of PAs (several Regions and
Divisions of WAPDA, 4 PIDAs, 4 PAD-OFWMs and many more AWBs and FOs) and the likelihood that
the project will consist of a large number of small contracts or packages (especially for Investment Projects
sponsored by FOs). Moreover, it is justified by the following circumstances: (i) the Borrower, WAPDA,
and Provinces have demonstrated experience and capacity in procurement matters on similar Bank-
financed projects; (ii) technical assistance would be provided under the project to support their
organizations and conduct prior review of procurement decisions of participating agencies; (iii) each
agency would execute a large number of similar repetitive contracts; (iv) IDA and other NDP donors
would conduct more intensive post reviews of procurement decisions based on documentation prepared by
the project's supervisory consultants; and (v) the Borrower's ability, and indicated willingness to accept
responsibility for the risk of misprocurement, resulting in cancellation of Credit proceeds.
20.    Post Review: The prior review will be complemented by post review of a random sample of
awarded contracts and procurement-related documentation below the prior review thresholds; in the
following proportions: (i) for works, I in 20 of an estimated 883 such contracts; (ii) for goods, I in 15 of
an estimated 125 such contracts; and (iii) for consultancy services, I in 5 of an estimated 100 such
contracts. The post review would cover the final contract and any evaluation of proposals and award
recommendations. In case misprocurement is detected during post review, IDA will immediately institute
a more intensive review of past and future contract documentation for procurement undertaken by the
concerned PA. Contracts financed under parallel financing arrangements (e.g., by OECF and ADB) would
also be subject to post review by IDA on a sample basis to ensure their compatibility with the balance of
the project, satisfactory quality, timely delivery or completion, and acceptable pricing.
21.    Review of Procurement Documents/Decisions in IDA: In most instances, IDA's review would
be carried out in the IDA's Resident Mission in Pakistan for completeness and adherence to IDA
procurement policies and guidelines. In cases where mandatory review is required by the IDA's Regional
Procurement Adviser or higher authority, an initial review would be carried out in the IDA's Resident
Mission in Pakistan for completeness and adherence to IDA procurement policies and guidelines, and
subsequently will be reviewed by the appropriate authority.

For Consultancy Services: $100,000 for firms and $50,000 for individuals with 98 percent value
coverage (100 percent for review of terms of reference)
Sample Post Review of Contracts Below Thresholds:
For Works: 1 in 20 of remaining 883 contracts
For Goods: 1 in 15 of remaining 125 contracts
For Consultancy Services: I in 5 of remaining 100 contracts

DISBURSEMENT ARRANGEMENTS
Statements of Expenditures (SOEs)
1.     Disbursement Against SOEs: IDA would disburse against Certified SOEs for the following types
of expenditures:
(a)    on contracts for works of less than $5,000,000 equivalent;
(b)    on contracts for equipments and vehicles of less than $300,000 equivalent;
(c)    on contracts for consultants services of less than $100,000 in the case of firms, and less
than $50,000 in the case of individuals;
(d)    for training expenditure; and
(e)    for incremental staff and operating costs.
All other expenditures would be supported by full documentation.
2.     SOE Documentation: Supporting documents for SOEs would not be submitted to IDA, but
would be retained by the PAs and be available to IDA during supervision. Each SOE would be supported
by a financial statement, separating investment and recurrent costs by expenditure category (such as civil
works, goods, and operating costs). Documentation for SOEs would include sufficient information to
enable IDA Supervision Missions to: (a) ensure an effective ex-post field review of documentation; (b)
verify and compare work performed, goods delivered, services provided, and payments made; (c) prepare
summary reports on detailed Investment Project information; and (d) meet IDA's requirements for
reporting source-of-supply information. If during implementation, IDA determines that the administrative
capacity of any PA is inadequate for complying with IDA's requirements for SOE documentation and
procedures, the NDP FMIS Unit would prepare and implement a plan for improvements.
3.     Annual Field Review of SOEs: Not later than six months after the end of each fiscal year of
project implementation, the NDP FMIS Unit would prepare for IDA's review, a report titled "Field Review
of SOE Documents" covering the entire the project. The objectives of the Review would be to: (a) verify
that expenditures are eligible for IDA financing; (b) establish the sufficiency and accuracy of supporting
documents maintained by the PAs for SOE disbursements; (c) assess, through discussions with independent
auditors, the continuing adequacy of procedures, systems, and controls used to monitor expenditures; (d)
ensure that the procurement procedures outlined in the Credit Agreement are being followed; and (e)
ensure that the required arrangements for timely independent audit of SOEs have been made.
Special Accounts
4.     Special Accounts:  To facilitate disbursements, Special Accounts in US Dollars would be
established in the National Bank of Pakistan, as follows:
(a)    Ministry of Water & Power: the Secretary, MW&P, Islamabad, with an initial deposit of
up to $100,000, to finance the costs of Federal Coordination and Supervision. The initial
deposit would be $50,000 until the aggregate deposits into this Special Account equal
$200,000;
(b)    WAPDA:
(i)    the General Manager (Finance) in Lahore, with an initial deposit of up to $2
million, to finance the costs of WAPDA Coordination, Institutional Reforms for
WAPDA's Water Wing and the Sector Planning and Research Component. The
initial deposit would be $1 million until the aggregate deposits into this Special
Account equal $4 million;



77                                    ANNEX 5
Page 2 of 2
(ii)   the General Manager (Water-South), in Hyderabad, with an initial deposit of up
to $5 million, to finance the costs of the Investment Component in Sindh
executed by WAPDA. The initial deposit would be $2.5 million until the
aggregate deposits into this Special Account equal $10 million;
(c)    Province of Sindh: the NDP Provincial Coordinator, Sindh Province, in Karachi or
Hyderabad, with an initial deposit of up to $5 million, to finance the costs of Provincial
Coordination, Institutional Reforms for PIDs, and Investment Component in Sindh
executed by the Province of Sindh. The initial deposit would be $2.5 million until the
aggregate deposits into this Special Account equal $10 million;
(d)    Province of Punjab: the NDP Provincial Coordinator, Punjab Province, in Lahore, with
an initial deposit of up to $2 million, to finance the costs of Provincial Coordination,
Institutional Reforns for PIDs, and the costs of the Investment Component in Punjab
Province executed by the Province of Punjab. The initial deposit would be $1 million
until the aggregate deposits into this Special Account equal $4 million;
(e)    NWFP: the NDP Provincial Coordinator, NWFP, in Peshawar, with an initial deposit of

and Institutional Reforms for PIDs in Balochistan Province executed by the Province of
Balochistan. The initial deposit would be $0.25 million until the aggregate deposits into
this Special Account equal $1 million.
5.     Expenditures to be Financed from the Special Account: The Special Account would be used to
finance all expenditures eligible for financing from the IDA Credit; and would not be used to finance
ineligible expenditure (such as duties and taxes, land acquisition, interest during construction, etc.).
6.     Replenishment: Withdrawal Applications for replenishment of the Special Account would be
submitted on a monthly basis, or when 20 percent of the Special Account has been utilized, whichever
occurs earlier.

ELIGIBILITY CRITERIA FOR PARTICIPATING AGENCIES (PAs)
1.     Except as IDA shall otherwise agree, each Participating Agency (PA) would satisfy the relevant
eligibility criteria to be eligible for incremental financing commitments from the IDA Credit for new
programs of activities to be commenced under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for
on-going Investment Projects. The eligibility criteria are outlined below.
2.     PIDAs, AWBs and FOs: Each PIDA, AWB and FO would satisfy the criteria indicated below to
be eligible for incremental financing commitments from the IDA Credit for new programs of activities to
be commenced under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for on-going Investment
Projects:
(a)    it has been established and is being operated as an autonomous entity;
(b)    it has signed a Participation Agreement, satisfactory to IDA, with the Province;
(c)    it has prepared and agreed with the NDP Coordination Cell a "Three Year Rolling
Business Plan for the PA's activities under the Project for the Fiscal Year and the two
next following Fiscal Years. The Plan shall demonstrate:
(i)    in case of a PIDA and an AWB, that the PIDA and AWB shall be financially
self-sustainable, so as to generate sufficient income (from all sources and
beneficiaries) to meet its O&M costs, operating costs, depreciation of assets, and
payments for irrigation and drainage services obtained by it', within a period not
exceeding ten years from date of establishment; and
(ii)    in case of an FO, that the FO shall be financially self-sustainable, so as to
generate: (aa) sufficient income (from all sources and beneficiaries) to meet its
O&M costs, operating costs, depreciation of assets, payments for irrigation and
drainage services obtained by it', and debt service payments; and (bb) sufficient
funds from its own resources and/or borrowings to meet its capital expenditures,
within a period not exceeding seven years from date of establishment.
(d)    it has achieved satisfactory progress in implementation of its Business Plan for the
previous Fiscal Year including:
(i)    achieving the projected (target) level of O&M expenditure; and
(ii)    achieving the projected (target) level of cost reduction, Abiana collection, and
cost sharing (beneficiary contributions).
(e)    it has appointed a firm/firm(s) of Chartered Accountants as independent auditors. The
firn of Chartered Accountants would be selected from the short-list of firms approved by
the Provincial NDP Cell; and
(f)    it has submitted to the NDP Coordination Cell unqualified Audited Financial Statements
for all completed fiscal years.
payment for irrigation and drainage services obtained would be made to upper-tier organizations,
e.g.: in case of an AWB, the upper-tier entity would be a PIDA.



79                                      ANNEX 6
Page 2 of 2
3.     PAD-OFWMs: Each PAD-OFWM would satisfy the criteria indicated below to be eligible for
incremental financing commitments from the IDA Credit for new programs of activities to be commenced
under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for on-going Investment Projects:
(a)    it has prepared and agreed with the NDP Coordination Cell a "Three Year Rolling
Business Plan for its activities under the Project for the Fiscal Year and the two next
following Fiscal Years;
(b)    it has achieved satisfactory progress in implementation of ils Business Plan for the
previous Fiscal Year including achieving the projected (target) level of cost sharing
(beneficiary contributions);
(c)    it has appointed a firm/firm(s) of Chartered Accountants as independent auditors. The
firm of Chartered Accountants would be selected from the short-list of firms approved by
the Provincial NDP Cell; and
(d)    it has submitted to the NDP Coordination Cell unqualified Audited Financial Statements
for all completed fiscal years.
4.     WAPDA: WAPDA's Water Wing would satisfy the criteria indicated below to be eligible for
incremental financing commitments from the IDA Credit for new programs of activities to be commenced
under the Project, and any new contracts to be awarded by it for on-going Investment Projects:
(a)    it has achieved progress, satisfactory to IDA, in the carrying out of its institutional reform
activities as agreed with IDA for the last preceding Fiscal Year of project implementation
(particularly on the strategic re-orientation and commitment to withdraw gradually from
construction of intra-Provincial drainage);
(b)    it has prepared and agreed with the NDP Coordination Cell on a "Three Year Rolling
Business Plan" for its activities under the Project for the Fiscal Year and the two next
following Fiscal Years;
(c)    it has achieved satisfactory progress in implementation of its Business Plan for the
previous Fiscal Year including:
(i)    meeting the projected (target) level of O&M expenditure; and
(ii)    meeting the projected (target) level for Abiana collection and cost sharing
(beneficiary contributions).
(d)    it has appointed a firm/firm(s) of Chartered Accountants as auditors for the project
beginning with FY96/97; and
(e)    it has submitted to the NDP Coordination Cell unqualified Auclited Financial Statements
for all completed fiscal years.
5.     The NDP Coordination Cell would verify and submit the necessary evidence (in structured tabular
format) to IDA regarding each PA, not later than March 31 of each year as part of the Consolidated
Business Plan for the project.

AGREED ACTION PLAN
PREAMBLE
I.     This Agreed Action Plan sets out the actions which would be taken by the Borrower, Provinces
and the PAs during the implementation of the project. The Action Plan would be implemented during the
course of the project. The actions to be implemented each year would be discussed and fnalized during
annual discussions on the Business Plans and the NDP Portfolio Performance Review.
GENERAL
2.     Policy Actions: Except as IDA shall otherwise agree, the Borrower and all Participating Agencies
(PAs), in consultation with IDA, would implement the actions committed to IDA by the Government of
Pakistan (GOP) in the Borrower's Sector Development Policy Letter dated August 20, 1995 and in the
Supplementary Sector Development Policy Letter dated October 3, 1995.
SECTOR PLANNING AND RESEARCH
Sector Planning
3.     Planning Studies: The Borrower, WAPDA, in consultation with IDA, would carry out the
following sector planning studies: (i) Irrigation and Drainage Atlas of Pakistan; (ii) Revenue Options for
WAPDA's Water Wing; (iii) Three Year Rolling NDP Public Sector Development Programs; (iv) Annual
NDP Portfolio Performance Reviews; (v) Efficacy of Past Drainage Investments; and (vi) Ninth Five Year
Plan.
4.     Feasibility Studies: The Borrower, Provinces, and WAPDA, in consultation with IDA, would
carry out the following feasibility studies: (i) for Investment projects which would be implemented under
the Investments Component; (ii) LBOD Stage II; and (iii) the follow-up project to NDP. WAPDA would,
in consultation with IDA also carry out the pre-feasibility study for the National Surface Drainage System
(NSDS); and if the pre-feasibility study confrms the NSDS's viability, carry out the full feasibility study
(including an Environmental Assessment and Resettlement Plan), financing plan, and legal framework for
its operation.
5.     National Water Policy: The Borrower, in consultation with IDA, would: (i) issue a broad Water
Policy Statement, which would provide an interim framework prior to the formulation of a comprehensive
policy; and (ii) prepare and issue a comprehensive "National Water Policy" to provide an appropriate
framework for water resources management.
6.     Regulation of Fresh Groundwater Exploitation: The Borrower, WAPDA and Provinces would,
in consultation with IDA: (i) introduce legislation to regulate fresh groundwater exploitation; and (ii)
strengthen regulatory capacity and enforcement during implementation of NDP.
7.     The Borrower, WAPDA and Provinces would undertake, in consultation with IDA, all the major
sector planning and policy studies which the Borrower has committed to IDA in its Sector Policy
Development Letter, including: (i) a National Salinity Survey; (ii) a study on pricing and distribution
policy on gypsum; and (iii) a study on water rights. WAPDA and Provinces would implement the
recommendations of the study on water rights in the pilot FO areas.
8.     Capital Cost Recovery: The Borrower and Provinces would formulate, in consultation with
IDA, proposals to ensure that recovery of capital costs is linked to benefits derived from the project
especially for large landholders.



81                                      ANNEX 7
Page2of 12
9.     NDP Sector Planning and Studies Consultants: The Borrower and WAPDA would engage the
NDP Sector Planning and Studies Consultants with qualifications, Terms of Reference, and staffing
satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998.
Research
10.    Major Research Programs: WAPDA would undertake the research programs which are
proposed to be financed under the project, in consultation with IDA, including the following (the
sponsoring institutions are indicated in brackets): (a) Design and Maintenance of Surface Drains (ISRIP);
(b) Hydrologic Design of Surface Drains (IWASRI and CEWRRE); (c) Collaborative (Community) Pilot
Tile Drainage (DRIP); (d) Institutional Framework for Improved Sustainability and Productivity of
Irrigated Agriculture in Pakistan (IIMI and IFPRI); (e) A Sectoral Approach to Resource Monitoring using
GIS (WAPDA's Drainage Monitoring and Evaluation Organization); (f) Reuse and Disposal of Drainage
Water (IWASRI); (g) Impact of Pipe Drainage Systems on Land and Water (IWASRI); and (h) Hydraulic
and Salinity model of the Indus River System (CEWRE). Provincial Irrigation and Drainage Research
Institutes would also be eligible to participate in the research program.
11.    Funding for Participating Research Institutes: The Borrower would maintain its financing for
Participating Research Institutes (PRIs) at a level at least equal to the FY93/94-95/96 average in real terns.
INSTITUTIONAL REFORMS
Institutional Reforms for WAPDA's Water Wing
12.    Institutional Reforms: WAPDA would implement its Institutional Reforms Program for its
Water Wing laid out in its letter to IDA dated July 30, 1995, in consultation with IDA. WAPDA would: (i)
submit to, and agree with IDA, a detailed Action Plan with a schedule for its Institutional Reforms Prograrn
to IDA; and (ii) implement the Action Plan.
13.    Streamlining: WAPDA, in consultation with IDA, would carry out the following actions:
a)     one or more comprehensive assessments of its own institutional capacity and the
utilization and development of that capacity;
b)     prepare plans to address identified constraints;
c)     implement actions to increase the degree of decentralization of authority and
responsibility to line managers and field offices, shorten the procurement review and
approval cycle, streamline operations of field offices, and improve the coordination and
organization of its research effort;
d)     formulate new  service regulations and personnel policies to improve operational
efficiency including staffing and recruitment policies;
e)     streamline  key  operations,  including  procurement  procedures  and  contract
administration, accounting and financial management, and operations and maintenance
of federal irrigation and drainage infrastructure;
f)     if necessary, design and implement a manpower transition. program to address the
concems of staff and labor of WAPDA's Water Wing which may arise in the course of
implementing the Water Wing's Institutional Reforms Program, and to assist their
transition into other aspects of WAPDA's operations or elsewhere outside the
organization, in order to ease the burden which this institutional program may impose on
the staff and managers;



82                                     ANNEX 7
Page3of 12
g)     restructure its Planning Division, starting with the various Departments/Cells concerned
with monitoring and research by reorganizing them in order to provide a more coherent
arrangement and avoid duplication, by implementing the recommendation of the NDP
Feasibility Study Consultants' Report, for example by: (a) locating all M&E, research,
and studies units under a newly established Senior Manager - the General Manager
(Monitoring and Research) - who would also control the SCARPs Monitoring
Organization (SMO), Watercourse Monitoring and Evaluation Directorate (WMED), the
International Waterlogging and Salinity Research Institute (IWASRI), Mona Research
Station, and the Lower Indus Water Management and Reclamation Research Institute
(LIM); (b) discontinuing benefit monitoring by SMO, reassigning the function to
WMED, and reconstituting WMED as the Directorate General of Benefit Evaluation; and
(c) merging the Soil Reclamation Directorate (SRD) into the Soil Survey Unit of SMO;
h)     carry out O&M of inter-Provincial infrastructure, and  other infrastructure which is
intended to be maintained by the O&M Directorate of WAPDA's Water Wing, on the
basis of multi-year O&M Performance Contracts. This would be subject to identification
of financing mechanisms; and
i)     make special efforts to employ women in as many professional and leadership positions
as possible, particularly where this facilitates interaction with and participation of women
beneficiaries.
14.    Capacity Building: WAPDA's Water Wing, in consultation with IDA, would:
a)     engage specialists and other consultants as needed to assist WAPDA to:
i)     formulate, codify, and publish its operational policies;
ii)    implement the project's Environmental Management Plan (EMP), Wetlands
Management Plan (WMP);
iii)    prepare Environmental Impact Assessments (ElAs), Environmental Action
Plans (EAPs) for Investment Projects implemented by WAPDA or other
agencies, and strengthen its Environmental Cell (WEC);
iv)    strengthen its monitoring and evaluation (M&E) functions;
v)     conduct physical, performance, portfolio, socioeconomic, and environmental
monitoring of drainage projects throughout the Indus Basin;
vi)    design and implement a multimedia public awareness and communication
campaign to encourage behavioral change among opinion leaders and policy
makers by raising public awareness about the causes, dangers, and remedies of
waterlogging and salinity, and the consequences of over-irrigation;
vii)   encourage public participation in projects implemented by its Water Wing;
viii)   promote effective demand for drainage services offered by the project; and raise
public awareness at the national level of the environmental implications of
drainage partly by integration of waterlogging and salinity in the environmental
education curriculum;
ix)    review and improve its procurement and contract administration systems;



33                                       ANNEX 7
Page 4 of 12
x)     strengthen financial management in its Finance Division;
xi)    strengthen information systems management, including by establishment of a
NDP Project Information System (NDPIS), Water Sector Information System
(WSIS) and Water Sector Portfolio Information System. (WSPIS);
xii)    strengthen its Planning Division;
xiii)   encourage the private sector to participate in irrigation amd drainage; and
xiv)    strengthen its training functions.
b)      establish':
i)     an Operations Policy Cell to strengthen its capaciity for formulating and

ii)    an autonomous Evaluation Cell which would report to lthe Authority through the

operations and policies;

development, including land acquisition, resettlement, social assessments,

and coordinate participation and gender initiatives under the Project. WAPDA
would also appoint a Senior Adviser, NGO Coordination to provide momentum
to and coordinate partnerships with NGOs under the Project;
iv)    a Public Information Center and Library to establish an. institutional capacity for
collecting, storing, retrieving and sharing with the public, information and data
pertaining to Pakistan's water resources;
v)     a Publications Cell to strengthen its capacity to produce quality publications and
reports, including production and editing for project-related and operational
reports, technical and professional publications; and
vi)    a Private Sector Partnership Cell to strengthen partnerships with the private
sector, on planning, selection and design of projects; and on Operation and
Maintenance. WAPDA would appoint a Senior Adviser, Private Sector
Partnership to provide momentum to and coordinate private sector partnership
aspects under the Project.
The objectives of establishing the Cells listed above may also be achieved by other alternative organizational
arrangements to be made by WAPDA in consultation with the Borrower and IDA.



84                                     ANNEX 7
Page 5 of 12
Institutional Reforms for PIDs
15.    Decentralization and Management Transfer: Provinces would implement the Institutional
Reforms Program for Provinces (decentralization and management transfer) in accordance with the
principles laid out in GOP's Sector Development Policy Letter to IDA dated August 20, 1995, the
Supplementary Policy Letter dated October 3, 1995.
16.    Review of PIDA Statute: The Borrower and Provinces would annually review the PIDA
Ordinance based on the experience of implementation, and would agree with IDA, ADB and OECF on any
amendments and improvements to the Statute.
17.    Functions of AWBs: The Borrower and Provinces would agree on the functions and powers of
the AWBs with IDA by June 30, 1997. The functions and powers of the AWB would be consistent with
the provisions of the PIDA Ordinance, and would inter alia include: (i) to receive irrigation water supplies
from the PIDA at the canal headworks and deliver the same to the various FOs falling within its territorial
jurisdiction on distributary/minor basis or to any other entity; (ii) to receive the drainage effluent from the
various FOs or any other entities located within its territorial jurisdiction and convey the same through
relevant drains constructed for this purpose; (iii) to establish the rate at which it will supply irrigation water at
its disposal to the various FOs located within its territorial jurisdiction after due consultation with the
Provincial Government and FOs concerned; (iv) to formulate and implement policies with a view to achieve
and continuously improve effective, economical and efficient utilization of irrigation water at its disposal on a
financially and environmentally sustainable basis; (v) to operate and maintain the irrigation and drainage,
storage reservoirs and flood control infrastructure located within its territorial jurisdiction and to plan, design,
construct and/or improve the same to ensure supply of irrigation water to water users within its jurisdiction
and conveyance and/or disposal of drainage effluent on reasonable and efficient basis; (vi) to execute,
implement and maintain, after prior written agreement as to the relevant terms and conditions and the extent
and mode of payment for the same, such scheme(s) as may be entrusted to it by the PIDA or by any agency or
entity of the Government; (vii) to establish criteria and procedures for granting, modifyring, reassigning,
renewing, suspending or revoking any concessions, licenses or subleases granted by it to any FO or other
person as well as for the management of the infrastructure in the event of suspension or revocation of a
concession, license or sublease; (viii) to formulate and implement policies with a view to ensuring that within
a period not exceeding ten years from the date of its constitution it becomes fully operative as a self supporting
and financially self sustaining entity for O&M costs; and (ix) in close cooperation with the Transition Wing of
the PIDA, adopt and implement policies aimed at promoting formation, growth and development of FOs.
18.    Coordinating Agency: Provinces would designate their Planning and Development Departments
or Planning and Development Boards (P&DDs), as the Provincial NDP Cells, to coordinate and oversee the
decentralization and management transfer process.
19.    Decentralization and Management Transfer Process:  Each Province would prepare and
implement the decentralization and management transfer (MT) process including: (a) delineating the
physical boundaries of the proposed PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs taking into account hydraulic features of the
irrigation schemes, social aspects, and economies of scale which apply; (b) outlining the rights and
obligations of PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs and drafting applicable Statutes including the necessary rules and
regulations, constituting PIDAs, AWBs and FOs; (c) formally registering those PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs
that are formed under the project with the appropriate authority; (d) facilitating the involvement of users
and the farming community at large in formulating the transfer program, its objectives, and process; (e)
organizing farmers into FOs, and conducting or overseeing elections of office bearers; (f) formalizing
"Titles of Leasehold" for the infrastructure to FOs, AWBs and PIDAs; (g) carrying out inventories of
machinery and equipment, including lists of assets to be transferred and assessments of the need for
additional equipment and/or repair of existing equipment; (h) preparing instruction manuals and
operational handbooks for PIDAs, AWBs and FOs, and master plans for rehabilitating or modernizing the
infrastructure, the related financial plans and policies to ensure financial viability, and detailed
programs/schedules for the transfer; (i) preparing and implementing training programs in which PIDAs,



85                                      ANNEX 7
Page 6 of 12
AWBs, and FOs jointly determine their technical and training needs; (j) carrying out the physical and legal
transfer of the system, infrastructure, machinery and equipment to the PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs; and (k)
implementing a Staffing, Operational and Financial Plan designed to address the concerns of staff and
labor of PIDAs which may arise, and where necessary, to assist their transition into other aspects of the
new entities' operations or elsewhere in order to ease the burden which the Institutional Program may
impose on the staff.
20.    Depending on technical and other considerations for viability, Provinces would establish AWBs
on each of Pakistan's canal commands, or on a combination thereof, beginning with pilots. Provinces
would also establish village-level FOs under the transition of FGW tubewells Investment Projects and
distributary level FOs. The overriding criteria for design of the distributary level FOs would be to establish
them at such sizes that would enable them to employ modern management skills, equipment, and
technology, optimize economic efficiency and financial viability, and equip/enable them to negotiate and
fulfill contract terms with AWBs and banks, subject to appropriate hydraulic and sociological limitations.
21.    Organization and Functions: Provinces would: (i) maintain PIDAs, AWBs and FOs under
organizational structures, functions, statutes, staffing, regulatory framework, all satisfactory to IDA, for the
period of project implementation and post-completion monitoring; and (ii) promptly inform IDA of any
proposed change in the organizational structures, functions, statutes, staffing, or regulatory framework.
22.    Streamlining and Cost Reduction in Operations of Decentralized Irrigation Institutions:
PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs would implement measures aimed at reducing O&M costs, and thereby reduce the
cost recovery base including: (a) formulating new service regulations and personnel policies; (b)
streamlining machine operations; (c) updating and revising service and technical manuals; (d) improving
accounting and financial management systems; (e) conducting specific diagnostic analyses and implement
subsequent action plans to streamline operations of selected drainage circles; (f) streamlining financing and
utilization of the O&M budget - inter alia by linking O&M financing with collection of Abiana (the
financing aspect of streamlining) and increasing the share of works in the budget (the utilization aspect of
streamlining) in selected pilot areas; (g) streamlining implementation of off-farm drainage O&M through
Performance Contracts (PCs) or Rehabilitate and Operate Contracts (ROCs) or other scheme awarded to
the private sector on competitive basis, and designating Drainage Circles for PCs; (h) initiating pilots to
test decentralization of Abiana assessment and collection during implementation of NDP, and designate
Circles where pilots to test decentralization of Abiana assessment and implementation would be
implemented; (i) rationalizing "Abiana" schedule; 0) building their capacities for delivery of services
under the new framework; transferring on-farm drains and tertiary drains to FOs and WUAs; and (k)
transitioning as many FGW tubewells as possible.
23.    Manuals: Provinces would: (i) prepare a "Manual of Operations" that would be specific to the
requirements of each Province, PIDA, AWB or FO; (ii) prepare a "Manual of Regulations for Autonomous
Bodies" in consultation with PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs; and (iii) prepare a "Manual of Regulations for FGW
Exploitation" in consultation with FOs that would be specific to the requirements of each Province.
24.    Study on Procedure for Pricing for Irrigation and Drainage Services: The Borrower and
Provinces would conduct a study on procedures for pricing of irrigation and drainage services in the
decentralized irrigation and drainage system. The study would, inter alia, examine mechanisms for
consultations and negotiations between the parties concerned (i.e., PIDA and AWB, or AWBs and FOs).
The study would be completed by June 30, 1998 and be implemented in the pilot AWB and FO areas by
December 31, 1998.
25.    Delivery and Pricing for Wholesale Irrigation and Drainage Services: PIDAs, AWBs, and
FOs would design, testlpilot, and if successful, implement a system of demand, delivery, and payment of
wholesale irrigation and drainage services all based on advance planning prior to the agricultural seasons.
Under such a system, PIDAs would eventually deliver services to AWBs baseid on the aggregate demand
from them, while AWBs would do likewise based on aggregate demand from FOs, who would base theirs



86                                      ANNEX 7
Page 7 of 12
on the demand from WUAs. Payment would be determined through negotiations at these aggregate levels
as well; and losses (arising from operational inefficiencies arising from mismanagement and/or
overstaffing, non-recovery of charges; leakages due to corruption; or system losses due to excessive
seepage or poor maintenance) would be absorbed by the responsible parties, and not transmitted system-
wide. PIDAs would have the power to set water charges to AWBs only; and would sell wholesale
irrigation and drainage services to them on a full cost-recovery basis. PIDAs' receivables from individual
AWBs would be independent of AWBs' receipts. from FOs; and losses would not be transferred from one
AWB to another. PIDAs would compensate AWBs for services for which AWBs are not expected to
recover costs; or which they carry out at the behest or direction of PIDAs. AWBs would similarly set
wholesale charges and deliver services to, and obtain payment from, individual FOs; and FOs would do so
likewise with WUAs.
26.    Recruitment of Managing Directors and Senior Officers of PIDAs, AWBs and FOs: PIDAs
and AWBs would recruit Managing Directors and Senior Officers from PIDs and/or the market through
transparent processes (i.e., including by advertising in the press, and the use of specialized professional
management recruitment firms). Managing Directors and Senior Officers would be acceptable to IDA.
27.    Accountability, Efficiency, and Autonomy: PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs established as part of the
project's Institutional Reform Program would be: (i) audited by Chartered Accountants appointed in
consultation with IDA; and (ii) established and run in accordance with generally accepted business
practice, under which Owners (whether Provinces or farmers), Board of Directors, and Management would
be completely separate.
28.    Regulatory and Corporate Oversight: Provinces would (i) establish a Policy & Regulation
Wing of PIDAs when existing PIDs are decentralized into PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs; (ii) assign
responsibility for establishing policy and regulating the operations of entities in the sector to the Wing; and
(iii) prepare and agree with IDA the regulatory and corporate oversight mechanism for the decentralized
irrigation and drainage system by December 31, 1997.
29.    Legal Cell: Each PIDA would establish a Legal Cell with Terms of Reference and staff,
including Chief Legal Counsel/Officer, agreed with IDA, by December 31, 1997, to advise on regulatory
and legal matters relating to the decentralized irrigation and drainage system.
30.    Water Allocation Committees: To improve the transparency of allocation of irrigation supplies,
each PIDA, AWB, and FO would establish, a "Water Allocation Committee, or WAC" for each point of
off-take (i.e. from barrages to canal headworks, from headworks to distributaries, and from distributaries to
watercourses). The WACs would publish annually or more regularly in the local press and in the
Provinces' or Districts' official gazette the allocations of irrigation supplies, with comparisons of
rated/authorized versus actual allocations.
31.    Construction Partnership and Handover Agreements:  WAPDA would sign framework
"Construction Partnership and Handover Agreements" with PIDAs, AWBs, and FOs for which it intends to
construct facilities and which would later be handed over to them.



87                                       ANNEX 7
Page 8 of 12
PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION
32.    Business Plan: All PAs would prepare and implement "Three Year Rolling Business Plans". The
Plan would include procurement, staffing, operations, and financing plans.
33.    Project Preparation Guidelines: The Borrower's Planning Commission (Water Wing) would
update guidelines for selection, preparation, and evaluation of irrigation and drainage investment projects
to include "basin orientation", and to explicitly integrate social, environment, resettlement, handover, and
post-completion O&M aspects.
34.    Provincial NDP Cells: Provinces would establish Provincial NDP Cells, each of which would be
headed by Provincial NDP Coordinators appointed by the ACS Development/Chairman of the P&DD
Board with responsibility for day-to-day coordination and supervision of the project in the Province on
behalf of the ACS (Development)/Chairman P&D Board. Provinces would re:locate the Provincial NDP
Cells to P&DDs in order to reflect more closely the multi-agency design of the project.
35.    Procurement Management2: WAPDA, in consultation with IDA, would: (i) establish an NDP
Procurement Unit with terms of reference, staffing from WAPDA and procurement consultants and budget;
(ii) appoint one or more consultants with internationally recognized professional qualifications in
procurement administration as NDP Procurement Advisers; (iii) delegate final approval authority for all
procurement for civil works contracts below $20 million, goods contracts below $10 million, and
consultancy contracts below $10 million which are financed under the project and implemented by
WAPDA to a "NDP Procurement Review Sub-committee" of the Authoriity established under the
respective General Manager, and with representation from the NDP Procurement Unit; and (iv) delegate
powers to the NDP Program Coordinator to approve up to 80 percent of the procurement values which are
expected to require WAPDA's approval under the project.
36.    Procurement Plans: (i) WAPDA and Provinces will prepare detailed Three-Year Rolling
Procurement Plans as part of their Three-Year Rolling Business Plans; (ii) the NDP Coordination Cell in
WAPDA will consolidate the procurement plans of participating agencies, and submit the combined Three-
Year Rolling Procurement Plan for IDA's review and approval annually by March 31, together with the
project's Combined Business Plan; and (iii) Contracts for civil works will be considered only as part or
parts of complete Investment Projects and be awarded only after the Investment Projects have been
approved by IDA.
37.    Disbursements: The NDP FMIS Unit (an organizational arm of the NDP Coordination Cell and
NDP Provincial Cells) would prepare and submit Withdrawal Applications for eligible expenditures
financed by PAs to IDA within 180 days of the date of incurring the expenditure. Eligibility for such
expenditures for financing under the Credit would be limited to the cut-off date of 180 days. Where Special
Accounts are established or used, the Replenishment Applications would be subnmitted on a monthly basis.
38.    Community Supervision: All PAs would establish Community Advisory Committees (CACs)
on various issues which require the local knowledge, advisory inputs and active participation of NGOs,
farmers' associations, local community leaders and other stakeholders to help them manage better the
interface of the project with impacted communities including, but not limited to, land acquisition,
2      Since Negotiations, WAPDA has proposed the following alternative arrangement: "WAPDA in consultation
with IDA, would: (i) establish an NDP Procurement Unit with staffing from WAPDA, Procurement Consultants and
Finance; (ii) appoint a Consultant with internationally recognized professional qualification in procurement
administration as NDP Procurement Adviser; and (iii) constitute an NDP Procurement Rleview Committee headed by
the Regional General Manager comprising the Project Consultants and the NDP Project Manager or his representative
to carry out one step evaluation of procurement contracts including works, goods and consultancy, where applicable.
The report of this Committee will be reviewed by CCC before approval from Managing Director (Water) or the
Authority as the case may be".



88
ANNEX 7
Page 9 of 12
environment, protection of local wetland resources and similar interventions which may be important to the
livelihoods of local communities.
39.    NDP Consultants: WAPDA would appoint one or more firms as NDP Consultants (including,
but not limited to, NDP Engineering Design and Supervision Consultants; and NDP Sector Planning and
Studies Consultants collectively referred to as NDP Consultants) to provide direct supervision of, and
implementation assistance to the PAs. WAPDA would cause NDP Consultants to establish a collective
Board of Management (BOM) consisting of the representatives of the organizations represented in the
NDP Consultants for coordination and supervision, and which would meet quarterly to review
implementation progress and deal with issues that may arise. WAPDA's General Manager (Planning)
would be an ex-officio member of the Board of Management. WAPDA would cause the Team Leaders of
the NDP Consultants to establish an Executing Committee, to which the BOM would delegate its
responsibilities and which would meet monthly.
40.    NDP Client Service Teams: WAPDA would ensure that staff of the NDP Units in WAPDA
Divisions (e.g. NDP Coordination Cell, FMIS Unit, NDP Procurement Unit/Cell, Social Cell), and of NDP
Consultants are deployed to assist or serve PAs only at the written request of the Chief Executive or
authorized representative of the PA. WAPDA would cause NDP Consultants, the PA's representative, and
counterpart staff of WAPDA Divisions' NDP Units to form "NDP Client Service Teams", whose task
would be to assist and supervise PAs on the basis of clear objectives, specific Terms of Reference, budgets,
schedules, and service indicators agreed between the NDP Coordination Cell and the PA's representative;
and which would be led by the representative of the PA (or failing, the nominee of the NDP Program
Coordinator).
41.    Evaluation Reports: The Chief Executives of PAs would complete one or more Evaluation
Reports using standardized formats, prepared by the NDP Coordination Cell (WAPDA) in consultation
with IDA, during and after the completion of each NDP Service Contract by the Client Service Team.
These evaluation reports would be compiled by the NDP Working Party with the assistance of NDP Sector
Planning and Studies Consultants.
42.    Operating Regulations: WAPDA's NDP Cell would formulate the Operating Regulations and
Manual of Procedures for the Project in close consultations with other PAs, and issue them to all PAs after
the endorsement of the Federal Program Steering Committee (FPSC) and IDA. The Operating
Regulations and Manual of Procedures would specify the general principles, terms and conditions for
financing under the project, roles and responsibilities of each PA, procedures for Investment Project
preparation and selection, eligibility criteria for PAs, eligible expenditures for financing, and a glossary of
terms. These Operating Regulations would be an integral part of the "Participation Agreement" to be
entered into between Provinces and PAs. WAPDA's NDP Cell would update the Operations Regulations
and Manual of Procedures periodically (at least annually).
43.    Participation Agreements: WAPDA (NDP Coordination Cell) and Provinces (Provincial NDP
Cells) would enter into "Participation Agreements" with PAs which are being financed by the project.
44.    Operational Manuals and Procedures: Each PA would develop detailed Operational Manuals
and Procedures in consultation with the NDP Design and Engineering Supervision Consultants for each
Investment Project; and submit them to IDA no later than one year prior to completion of the Investment
Project.
45.    Interest During Construction (IDC): The Borrower's Planning Commission would examine
and make modifications in the necessary procedures to ensure that IDC is capitalized and not deducted
during implementation; but is calculated at completion of Investment Projects and included in the final
project cost.



89                                      ANNEX 7
Page IO of 12
FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT AND INFORMATION SYSTEMS
46.    The NDP FMIS Unit: WAPDA would establish in its NDP Coordination Cell, or in its Finance
Division, a NDP Financial Management and Information Systems (FMIS) Unit headed by a Financial
Controller reporting to the General Manager (Finance) of WAPDA, which would have overall
responsibility for the Project Account(s). WAPDA would staff the NDP FMIS Unit with professionally
qualified accountants (i.e. Chartered Accountants), management specialists, and information systems
professionals.
47.    Financial Management and Information Systems (FMIS) Consultants: The General Manager
(Finance) of WAPDA would engage a firm of Chartered Accountants/Manageiment Consultants to assist
WAPDA and PAs improve their financial management, accounting, budgeting, and cost control systems;
and management information systems in all functional areas by June 30, 1998.
48.    General Manager-Finance of PIDAs and AWBs: Each PIDA and AWB would appoint a
professionally qualified accountant (i.e., Chartered Accountant or Cost Accountant) as General Manager-
Finance.
49.    Technical Assistance: WAPDA would, through the NDP FMIS Unit and the FMIS Consultants,
provide technical assistance to PAs in the preparation of their Financial Statements, verify and consolidate
them as part of their implementation assistance role on behalf of the Borrower, Provinces, and IDA. The
NDP FMIS Unit would prepare, maintain, and update "Consolidated Project Costs, Financing Plan, and
Accounts" for the entire project monthly, quarterly, annually, and cumulatively.
50.    Audit Arrangements: The Borrower, Provinces, and WAPDA would appoint a firm(s) of
Chartered Accountants to audit the Financial Statements for the project. PAs which fail to submit their
audited accounts within six months to the NDP FMIS Unit in WAPDA wouldL not be eligible for funds
from all project sources (i.e. Bank, the Borrower, Provinces, and other donors).
51.    Project Information Systems: The NDP FMIS Unit would develop a unified: (i) "Project
Financial Accounting and Management System"; (ii) "Project Information System (NDPIS)" which would
link the financial information system to all the project's activities and organization; and (iii) "Water Sector
Information System (WSIS)" linking the NDPIS to the socioeconomic, environrnental, infrastructural, and
hydrologic database of the project and the rest of the IBIS.
INFORMATION DISCLOSURE
52.    Project Policy: The Borrower, WAPDA, and Provinces would subscribe to the project's policy
and standards in favor of a high degree of public participation and disclosure of project information to the
public and the stakeholders in particular, inter alia, by endorsing a suitably worded generic statement
prepared by the NDP Coordination Cell to that effect. They would hold at Least one consultative and
informative public meeting in March before the formulation of the year's work program and budget; and
during the middle of the fiscal year to brief the stakeholders about the PA's progress in implementing the
year's work program and budget. The Participation Agreements with PAs would reflect the information
disclosure policy of the project i.e., a general presumption would exist in favor of public disclosure and
widespread dissemination of all of the project's formal/official reports, through publication of summary
leaflets and paid advertisements in local newspapers with translations in the local languages.
53.    Release of Documents of Public Interest: The Borrower, Provinces, and WAPDA would
translate the Drainage Sector Environmental Assessment (DSEA) and other project related documents of
public interest into local languages; summarize these documents and release them to the public before the
Mid-term Review through the media and Public Information Center and Library to be established by
WAPDA under the project. WAPDA would translate all "Three Year Rolling Business Plans" for PAs, all
RAPs, EIAs, and Investment Project Feasibility Study Reports into the local languages and disseminate



90                                       ANNEX 7
Page 11 of 12
them widely to stakeholders, including through the local press in English and Urdu. WAPDA would
arrange for the full ElAs and RAPs to be available in the local language on demand from affected
populations and NGOs.
54.    Annual Report and Audited Financial Statements: WAPDA would publish the Annual Report
and Audited Financial Statements, the Annual Monitoring and Evaluation (M&E) Report, and the
Environmental and Resettlement Report of the project as a whole, or substantive excerpts thereof, in the
local press; and hold at least one public hearing meeting with stakeholders (including farmers, staff and
contractors) in its Headquarters and Regional Offices to discuss the Annual Report and Audited Financial
Statements. Each PA would publish its Annual Reports in the local press, and hold at least one public
briefing meeting with its stakeholders to discuss its Annual Reports and Audited Financial Statements.
55.    Quarterly Bulletin/Newsletter:  The NDP Cells would publish and distribute nationally a
quarterly bulletin or newsletter to educate and inform the public and project-affected persons about the
project's objectives, activities, policies, programs, and achievements. The magazine or bulletin would
recognize and highlight significant achievements of individuals, PAs and other agencies in support of the
project's objectives.
56.    Radio and Television Programs: The GOP's MW&P, WAPDA and Provinces would sponsor or
facilitate radio and television programs to communicate the project's objectives to the public in such
regularity as they may deem appropriate.
57.    Public Information Center and Library (PICL): WAPDA's Water Wing would establish and
maintain a Public Information Center and Library (PICL) in Lahore, Regional Offices and other publicly
accessible offices of WAPDA, PIDAs, and AWBs, which would be used as collection, storage, and
dissemination centers for public information regarding the project, water resources development issues in
Pakistan in general, and participatory irrigation and drainage management (PIM). All PICLs would be
accessible/open to the public, particularly the academic community, PAs, NGOs, students, and the press.
The PICLs would contain up-to-date copies of project information, which would be prominently displayed
with the intention of attracting the interest of the reading public.
58.    Action Plan for Information, Public Communication, Education, and Participation: WAPDA
will submit and agree with IDA, and implement, a comprehensive Three Year Rolling Action Plan for
Information, Public Communication, Education, and Participation, prepared in collaboration with the
Borrower, Provinces and IDA, and with the assistance of development communication and media
professionals recruited under the project; and implement the program.
SOCIAL ASPECTS
59.    Private Sector Partnership, Participation and Gender Aspects: The Borrower, WAPDA, and
Provinces would: (i) pay particular attention to and promote partnerships with the private sector in the
selection, design, planning, implementation, and supervision of NDP; (ii) introduce public participation in
planning investment schemes and O&M during implementation of NDP; (iii) expand NGO role in
irrigation and drainage during implementation of NDP; (iv) pay particular attention to and promote
participation of women in the selection, design, implementation, and supervision of NDP; and (v) make
special efforts to employ women in as many professional and leadership positions as possible, particularly
where this would facilitate interaction with/participation of women beneficiaries.
60.    Social Assessments: WAPDA and Provinces would conduct Social Assessments (SAs) for all
Investment Projects and for FOs established under the project.
61.    Stakeholders Surveys:  WAPDA's Planning Division would conduct a formal survey of
stakeholders annually. Each survey would be presented to collective groups of PAs and to the public at



91                                     ANNEX 7
Page 12 of 12
public meetings within six months after the completion of every fiscal year. The reports would be
presented/packaged in dosages which have information that is likely to be of local interest.
62.    Resettlement: The Borrower would cause WAPDA and Provinces Ito adopt and publish the
Framework for Land Acquisition and Resettlement (FLAR) agreed with IDA for NDP as the policy for
land acquisition and resettlement under the project
ENVIRONMENTAL ASPECTS
63.    Environmental Impact Assessment: WAPDA  and Provinces would prepare ELAs for
environmentally-sensitive Investment Projects, which will include Environmental Action Plans (EAPs).
The EIAs will be submitted by the NDP Cells for approval by the respective Environmental Protection
Agency (EPA), and thereafter submitted to IDA and the directly concerned cofmancier for review and
approval, before a Investment Project is approved for funding. For identified Investment Projects,
Provincial EPAs, in collaboration with WAPDA's Environmental Cell and Provincial NDP Cells would
arrange for public consultations in coordination with EPAs, NGOs, and other relevant organizations.
Environmental Management Committees (EMCs) would be established for those Investment Projects
which require mitigating measures.
64.    Basin-wide Environmental Monitoring and Management:  The Borrower would cause
WAPDA and Provinces to prepare in consultation with the Provinces, and agree with IDA on the
following: (i) a program of policies and actions to strengthen environmental management; (ii) policy and
regulatory framework to monitor extraction of fresh groundwater aquifers and control intrusion of saline
groundwater into fresh groundwater aquifers, and disposal of industrial effluents into waterways; (iii) a
National Wetland Management Plan; and (iv) a program of studies, research, and capacity building under
NDP.
65.    Wetlands Management Plan (WMP):  (i) WAPDA and Provinces would implement the
project's WMP with due diligence; and (ii) any proposal to drain the Sindh Riverine areas, areas between
the main drains and the coast, flood plains, or lake shores, would be subject to full ELAs, in accordance
with Pakistan's Environmental Protection Laws and Bank policy, prior to seeking IDA's approval for the
Investment Project. WAPDA would take a lead role in the project's WMP.
66.    Effluent Disposal: WAPDA and Provinces would prepare and agree with IDA on: (i) a national
strategy for effluent disposal from the Indus Basin; and (ii) initiate the shift from drainage tubewells to sub-
surface tile drains systems during implementation of NDP.
67.    NDP Environment and Social Design Consultants:  WAPDA would engage the NDP
Environment and Social Design Consultants with qualifications, Terms of Reference, and staffing
satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998.
68.    Monitoring and Evaluation: WAPDA would establish and maintain an effective M&E
organization and system for the project as a whole; and to this end will collaborate with the Provinces.
69.    NDP M&E Consultants: WAPDA would engage the NDP M&E Consultants with qualifications,
Terms of Reference, and staffing satisfactory to IDA by June 30, 1998.
